Human Trafficking Case Cracked on the Shenyou Ship 180

The case involves Liu Shikui, a staff member of the Municipal Public Security Bureau

Liu Shikui, a staff member of the Second Section of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, suddenly went to the Household Registration Office of the First District and Second Precinct on the 19th of this month and told Chen Shusheng, the patrol officer there, that Xu, a Fujianese who works in a certain place under the Municipal Government, is well known to me. Xu has a fellow villager named Xu Yong'an, who lives in the Danfeng Road area. He has recently had important matters and plans to return to his hometown. Because he is carrying several pieces of luggage, he is afraid of being extorted and harassed by a group of hooligans at the pier. Therefore, he asked Xu to entrust me to take care of him. Because I did not know Xu's address and he would be taking a ship in the next few days, I came here to ask the patrol officer to check Xu's detailed address so that I could go and contact Xu, etc. Chen patrol officer immediately flipped through the household registration book and found that Xu Yong'an's house was located at No. 106 Danfeng Road. I will lead you if you want to go to answer. Section staff Liu replied that there is no need to trouble you. Please send a police officer to lead me there. Chen patrol officer then dispatched police officer Fang Liming to accompany Liu to Danfeng Road. At the same time, Liu also asked Chen to send a police officer to escort Xu to the pier when he goes to take the ship. Chen also agreed. Then, police officer Fang Liming led section staff Liu to the front door of Xu's house at No. 106 Danfeng Road. Later, he saw Liu enter, and police officer Fang returned to the station. Until the next day, Xu Yushu from No. 106 brought a child and several pieces of luggage, and police officer Fang escorted them to the pier. After seeing Xu and others step on the Shenyou ship docked at the Pudong, Fang bid farewell and returned to the station. Until about 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, Wen Hongen, the director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, received a secret report that Xu Yushu from Fujian was carrying a child on the Shenyou ship to Fujian to sell, etc. When the matter concerned trafficking in people, he immediately secretly ordered the Supervisory Office to send service personnel Lin Peng and Chen Tongming to join the water patrol captain to rush to the Pudong side of the South Wharf and board the Shenyou ship to inspect. They then found a man carrying a child in the cabin of the ship, which was very suspicious. They questioned him. They learned that the man was Xu Yushu. According to Xu, he is 41 years old this year, originally from Xinghua, Fujian Province, and currently lives at No. 106 Danfeng Road in Shanghai. The child's name is Mei Mei, and she is five years old this year. I bought her from Suzhou at my own expense. Now I plan to take her to Fujian to sell. I have notified the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Municipal Government, etc., and Liu Shikui, a staff member of the Second Section of the Public Security Bureau, also knows, and a police officer was sent to escort us here to board the ship. After he finished speaking, he took out a piece of section staff Liu's name card. After the officers read it, they took Xu and the child along with Liu's name card to the water patrol team. Director Zhu took the case for preliminary interrogation and handed over the witnesses to the Public Security Bureau for handling. Director Wen believed that the case was very important and it was necessary to send personnel to investigate the facts closely before further investigation.

County District Farmers Association Relieves Farmers' Suffering 181

Banning Illegal Overcollection of Land Rent

Yang Zhuoyun, the chief executive of the Third District Farmers Association of Shanghai County, recently because one or two landlords in the district, regardless of the poor harvest this autumn and the desolation of the people's livelihood, dared to violate the county order and make exceptional demands, collecting more than one yuan of silver per stone of land rent, so the executive meeting decided to report to the county government and order a reduction. The general farmers were all happy.

Apprehension of Robbers Who Shot and Wounded Three Police Officers in Huatongfang 182

Three Robbers Arrested in a Linchun Teahouse

At 7:40 AM on the 3rd of this month, several armed robbers broke into the home of Zhou Bocheng, a Yangzhou native residing at No. 4 Huatongfang, North Xizang Road. They brandished pistols, demanding silence, and robbed 20 yuan in paper money and two gold rings. As they were searching for more valuables, the Hongkou police station received a report and dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to apprehend them. The robbers, alert and cunning, forced their way out and fled wildly through areas like Manzhou Road and Kulun Road in Zhabei. Police officers No. 2073 Zhang Liankui, No. 2062 Zhou Peixin, and No. 2213 Liu Qingxin attempted to stop them. The robbers opened fire to resist arrest, shooting and injuring the three officers, who fell to the ground one after another, allowing the criminals to escape. Zhang, Zhou, and Liu were taken to Baolong Hospital by ambulance for treatment, but Officer Zhang succumbed to his injuries at 1:00 AM on the 8th. Subsequently, Hongkou Police Detective Shi En, along with Detective Bao Shuji, apprehended Zhou Maoxian (47 years old, from Yancheng), Lin Xiaogui (34 years old, from Qingjiang), and Wang Weichun (34 years old, from Yancheng), the robbers involved in the case, at the Linchun Teahouse on Jiujiang Road. Zhou confessed that a Mauser pistol with three bullets was hidden on the rooftop of No. 4, Lane 245, Kulun Road. Detectives secretly went there, along with detectives from the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, and retrieved the gun from under the roof tiles, taking it back to the police station for safekeeping. Yesterday, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that investigations revealed the group had gathered beforehand in room 27 of the Wuzhou Hotel on Guangdong Road to plan the robbery. They reconnoitered the area near Zhou's residence to identify escape routes and then went armed to carry out the robbery. The victim, Zhou Bocheng, and his wife, Ms. Yi, were still asleep when Zhou Maoxian and Lin Xiaogui went upstairs, using the pretext of searching for opium to wake the Zhou couple. They claimed there were 2,000 yuan in cash and demanded it be handed over quickly. They took two gold rings from Ms. Yi's fingers and 20 yuan in paper money from Zhou's wallet, but feeling it was not enough, they continued to search. When the police detectives arrived, the group took the opportunity to flee into the Chinese-controlled area, opening fire on the police as they escaped. The three defendants admitted at the police station that they went to rob the Zhou family of their property. Zhou confessed to firing several shots, knocking down the three officers. Lin and Wang denied firing the gun. The two stolen gold rings were hidden by Zhou at the residence of his mistress in Zhangjiaxiang village in Zhabei and have since been recovered. Police detectives recovered three bullets and three bullet casings at the scene of the incident on Manzhou Road and Kulun Road. The Western firearms expert, Ying Na, confirmed that they were fired from the recovered Mauser pistol. Yesterday, the victim Zhou Bocheng, rickshaw puller Wang A'er, and hotel tea servers Chen A'sheng and Wang A'jin all appeared in court to testify. The gun, bullets, and gold rings were presented for inspection. After hearing the testimony of the victim and witnesses, and the verification by Western expert Pang Na, defendant Zhou Maoxian readily admitted his guilt. Lin Xiaogui claimed he did not have a gun, and when escaping north from Manzhou Road in Zhabei, there was still a person named Wang in their group who was behind them. He heard gunshots. Wang Weichun admitted to going along with the robbery, but he did not enter the residence. After a while, he hired a rickshaw and fled from the Xiaocaichang area of Gongyi Lane in Zhabei. The remaining statements were evasive. Judge Wu Zehan ordered them to be remanded in custody for further investigation at a later date.

Ni Lu Appeals Her Adultery Conviction 183

Ni Shunrong, a villager near Baoxin An in Loutang, Jiading, had a modest family fortune. He married Ni Lu as his wife. Initially, they lived peacefully. However, in the spring of this year, Lu was seduced into an adulterous affair by Huang Baosheng, who lived nearby. As their passionate affair deepened, Huang Baosheng dared to bring a sharp blade on the night of May 17th (lunar calendar) and hid in Ni's house, plotting to murder Ni Shunrong so he and Lu could be together forever. That evening, Ni Shunrong entered the room, intending to sleep, when he heard a noise in the corner. He became suspicious, lit a lamp, and suddenly saw Huang Baosheng crouching there with a knife. Ni was terrified and shouted for help. Neighbors, thinking it was a fire, rushed over to investigate. Huang Baosheng, seeing that his plan had been exposed, ran away and disappeared. Afterward, Ni reported the incident to the local police station, who arrested Huang. After Huang was released upon completion of his prison term, Huang colluded with Lu and on August 21st (lunar calendar) they packed up and fled together. Ni Shunrong searched everywhere and eventually found Huang Baosheng and Ni Lu hiding at No. 2 Bianjiazhai in Jiangwan, living together as husband and wife. Ni reported this to the Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District, who sent police to the address. They arrested the adulterous couple in the bedroom and handed them over to the local court for interrogation. Huang Baosheng was sentenced to eight months in prison, and Ni Lu was sentenced to five months in prison, as a warning to others. Meanwhile, Ni Shunrong filed a lawsuit with the court, requesting a divorce, citing her adultery and fleeing, even plotting with her lover to murder him. He argued that if they were to continue living together, his life would be in danger. The court held a mediation hearing. Ni Lu stated that her husband wanted to take a concubine and also disliked her appearance. She did not want a divorce. Therefore, the mediation failed, and Ni was advised to file a formal lawsuit. Ni Lu was sent to prison to serve her sentence. It has now been learned that Ni Lu has appealed the criminal court's verdict to the local court, which has accepted her appeal and scheduled a hearing for January 6th.

Dr. Zhang Caisheng Opens a Branch Clinic 184

Dr. Zhang Caisheng, an ophthalmologist and surgeon, has been practicing medicine at Wenyuanfang, outside the Xiaobeimen in Shanghai, for over ten years. He has extensive experience and is particularly skilled in diagnosis. His patients have all benefited from his healing touch. At the request of friends, and to make it easier for patients to seek treatment, he has opened a branch clinic in Fushoufang, outside the Xiaoximen. Clinic hours are from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM and from 4:00 PM to 7:00 PM. He will continue to see patients at his main residence as well. Consultation fees remain the same.

Security Team Arrests Daylight Robber 185

The Third Team of the South Shanghai District Security Corps arrested a robber named Chen Fugeng, a 27-year-old from Suzhou, yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM. Chen snatched a silver necklace from A'shui, the five-year-old son of Gu Wenqiao, who was playing in the Sanshanli of Fushentang Street outside the Dananmen, and fled. Chen Chenfu and Wang Er, who witnessed the incident, chased after him, shouting "Thief!" Wang Yaozhang, a Security Corps member on duty, heard the alarm and reported it to the team. Voluntary Corps members, including Chen Zhiming, were immediately dispatched and apprehended the robber, recovering the stolen item. The team leader, Zhu Yunsheng, immediately summoned the victim, Gu Wenqiao, and witnesses Chen Shoufu, etc., to verify the facts. However, the robber Chen Fugeng's statements were evasive, and he refused to confess. The team prepared a letter and handed over the person and the stolen goods to the Third Precinct of the First District Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Renowned Fujian Painter Comes to Shanghai to Seek Refuge 187

Li Xia to Hold Solo Exhibition

Li Xia, a renowned painter from Xianyou, Fujian, also known as Yunxian and Suishi, came to Shanghai in the spring of 1919 to escape the devastation in his hometown. His large-scale paintings were praised by art connoisseurs in Shanghai and Hangzhou as the best of portraiture. He returned to Fujian in the winter of 1920. However, admirers in Shanghai repeatedly invited him to return, but to no avail. Due to the recent turmoil in Fujian, he has once again come to Shanghai to seek refuge and is residing at the Xing'an Guild Hall at Dadongmen. He is said to have brought over a hundred of his best works and will hold a solo exhibition at a selected location soon to seek critique and guidance from fellow artists.

Thirty-First Branch of the Municipal Federation Holds Meeting 188

Petition to Open Iron Gates on Boundary Roads

The Thirty-First District Branch of the First Special District Municipal Federation held its first executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Eighteen people attended, chaired by Song Shixiang. The following matters were discussed: (1) Distribution of duties and mutual election of standing committee members: Fei Liangheng, Zheng Dongshan, Song Shixiang, Shi Zhiyun, Yang Guanqing; General Affairs: Chen Boxiang, Zhang Keyou, Zhou Zhicheng; Organization: Chen Jiabao, Xu Zhifang, Zhang Junjiang, Ji Jianhua, Fei Qiujiang; Mediation: Gui Yanfang, Jiang Zhongying, Wang Biru; Publicity: Zhang Yuqing, Zhou Renqing, Xu Wenfu, Tang Linsheng; Director of General Affairs: Du Chunsu; Representatives to the Federation: Song Shixiang, Fei Liangheng, Yang Guanqing, etc. (2) Zhang Yongxing's house number was searched by patrol officers for no reason. The committee decided to send a letter and appoint Song Shixiang as the representative to negotiate with the police station. (3) Regarding the maintenance of local public safety and liaison, it was resolved to host a banquet for local authorities. (4) Several hundred shops on Kenehai Road on the Boundary Road requested the opening of the iron gates to maintain their livelihoods and facilitate traffic. It was resolved (A) to petition the Road Bureau and the Police Department as a final request. (B) To publish the plight of the merchants and seek the sympathy and assistance of all sectors of society, etc. The meeting adjourned at approximately 4:00 PM.

City Voices 189

▲The Popularity of Xuan Paper Cards Chinese Xuan paper is highly regarded by countries around the world, with even Sweden admitting its inferiority. This is a great honor for our country. It is a pity that its high price prevents it from being widely used. The Shanghai Family Industrial Cooperative has commissioned the paper mill to produce four-foot-wide imitation Xuan paper suitable for couplets, and after being mounted in multiple layers as cards, they are even more beautiful than Xuan paper from Anhui. The New Year's cards used by Mr. Bolede, the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, are made of this imitation Xuan paper, which has been praised by everyone who has seen them. Therefore, Chinese and Western people in the customs are competing to order prints from the cooperative. The use of imitation Xuan paper for cards is changing fashion. The Customs Commissioner has indeed made a contribution to promoting it, while our Chinese people are using Western paper instead, which is rather embarrassing in comparison.

Educational News from Other Ports

Shandong Province Principals' Meeting Concludes; Teachers' College Entrance Examination Decided 196

Training and Service Issues Also Resolved

(Jinan Quick News) The Shandong Education Department's provincial principals' meeting, which opened on the 20th, has been discussing issues related to the training and service of normal school students for several days. This morning (22nd) at 9:00 AM, the meeting continued, with all 27 principals in attendance, chaired by Ling Zhizhong and recorded by Zhang Zicai. After revising the outline of the training and service issues discussed yesterday, the discussion of the entrance examination began. At 11:00 AM, a break was taken, and a group photo was taken as a memento. The discussion continued at 1:30 PM and ended at 5:00 PM, at which time the meeting was adjourned. The principals, having completed the meeting, are scheduled to return to their respective schools within days. The revised original text of the training service outline and the entrance examination subjects are recorded below.

Training Issues 197

Training is divided into three major categories: A. Spiritual Training, B. Skills Training, C. Knowledge Training. (A) Spiritual Training: A. Principles: 1. Foster students' correct learning concepts, with seeking knowledge as the core of educational activities. 2. Cultivate students' professional attitude toward education. 3. Cultivate students' interest in rural life. 4. Cultivate students' perseverance. 5. Cultivate students' progressive and creative consciousness. 6. Cultivate students' sincere, amiable, and optimistic attitude. 7. Cultivate students' simple and diligent habits. 8. Cultivate students' group living habits. 9. Cultivate students' noble recreational habits. B. Methods: 1. Implement training in accordance with the current educational purposes. 2. Matters that students can handle themselves in daily life should not be done by workers, such as cleaning school buildings and sweeping courtyards. 3. If there are larger construction projects, students should work as much as possible within their capabilities. 4. Students should use domestic products and prohibit imported goods. 5. Student expenses should be determined by the school based on the local cost of living and students' families should be notified to strictly prohibit waste. 6. The school should provide practical leadership and strict examination of students' attitudes and actions, eliminating romantic and decadent habits. 7. Lead students to carry out rural activities. 8. Guide students to organize group activities, various academic and cooperative societies. 9. Use travel, recreation, and various competitions to inspire students' progressive spirit. (B) Skills Training: A. Essential Items: 1. Teaching skills should be adapted to the needs of rural primary school teaching. 2. Production skills: the ability to improve agriculture, promote agricultural and sideline industries, and handicrafts. 3. Organizational skills: the ability to assist in local autonomy, sanitation, cooperation, and other undertakings. B. Requests: 1. Pay attention to observation, practice, and teaching methods. 2. Schools should establish one or several courses in agriculture, animal husbandry, crafts, and home economics, depending on the location and nature of the school. The equipment and management costs will be paid from the education fund. 3. Use extension services to connect students with society and actively operate mass education or rural activity areas. 4. Emphasize health knowledge and training and guide students to carry out rural health activities. 5. Establish cooperatives to cultivate students' interest in running cooperative businesses and their ability to guide cooperation. C. Knowledge Training: Training should be carried out in accordance with the curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education, and attention should be paid to extension services and extracurricular activities to increase experience.

Service Issues 198

1. Implement the Ministry of Education's regulations on service for normal school graduates. 2. The Department of Education will order the Fifth Section of each county to contact the normal schools and rural normal schools when there is a shortage of primary school teachers and educational administrators. 3. The Department of Education will order the Fifth Section to replace unqualified teachers and educational administrators who are considered to have poor service performance by the inspectors with graduates from normal schools and rural normal schools as much as possible. 4. Graduates who achieve a grade of A in the graduation examination will be introduced by the Department of Education to better-paying positions in primary schools. 5. Implement service guarantees: 1. Teachers should not be arbitrarily replaced unless there is misconduct. 2. Those who have served continuously in one school for more than five years will be given the opportunity for appropriate advanced studies. Those who continue to serve after advanced studies will receive an annual salary increase. 3. Those who have served continuously in one school for more than fifteen years will have their children admitted to public schools in the province for free. 4. Those who have served continuously in one school for more than twenty years and are over the age of sixty and voluntarily retire will be given a pension. 5. Those who are injured on duty and cannot continue to work or die will be given a pension. 6. Detailed service guarantee measures will be determined by the Department of Education. 6. The Department of Education will establish a career introduction department. All normal school graduates without work can register for introduction. 7. Each normal school and rural normal school will establish an inquiry department. Graduates can directly inquire when they encounter difficulties in service. 8. During the annual holidays, the Department of Education or each normal school and rural normal school can organize academic lectures or training courses to provide primary school teachers with opportunities for advanced studies.

Examination Issues 199

A. Subjects: 1. Normal School Graduation Examination Subjects: 1. Party Principles: Premier's Testament. 2. Chinese Language: Composition, Editing, Chinese Language, General Knowledge. 3. History and Geography: Chinese and foreign history, Chinese and foreign geography. 4. Physics and Chemistry: General Physics and Chemistry. 5. Mathematics: Arithmetic, Algebra, Geometry and Trigonometry. In addition to Arithmetic, which is a required subject, students can choose two of Algebra, Geometry, and Trigonometry. 6. Biology: General Biology. 7. Introduction to Education, Educational Psychology. 8. Primary School Administration. 9. Primary School Teaching Materials and Teaching Methods. 2. Rural Normal School Graduation Examination Subjects: 1. Party Principles: The Three Principles of the People. 2. Chinese Language: Composition, Editing. 3. Mathematics: Arithmetic, Elementary Algebra, Plane Geometry. 4. Social Studies: Chinese and foreign history, Chinese and foreign geography. 5. Natural Science: Physics, Chemistry, Biology, Physiology, Hygiene. 6. Psychology. 7. Education: Rural Education, Teaching Methods, Primary School Administration. 8. Rural Society, Rural Economics, Rural Society. 9. Introduction to Agriculture. B. Student Internships and Extracurricular Activities: The Department of Education will pay special attention to this when inspecting the performance of normal schools and rural normal schools in the province. Each school will also conduct its own strict examination. Students who fail in the above two areas will not be allowed to graduate.

Ministry of Education Releases Report on Inspection of Six Shanghai Universities 200

Jinan University has worked hard to reorganize after the war, and is now gradually returning to its original state.

The spirit of running schools at Datong and Hujiang Universities is infused, and the Business School of Fudan University is developing well.

There is overlapping of departments and enrollment at each school, enrollment is not very strict, and many students are extravagant.

Previously, the Ministry of Education ordered Chen Kezhong, editor of the National Compilation and Translation Bureau, Zhang Shaozhong, professor at National Zhejiang University, and Xie Shuying, section chief, to go to Shanghai to inspect six universities: Jinan, Datong, Hujiang, Fudan, Guanghua, and Daxia. The aforementioned personnel have completed their reports and submitted them to the Ministry of Education. The following is an excerpt of the main points of the original inspection reports. It is also heard that the Ministry of Education has copied and distributed the reports and highlighted key points, ordering improvements.

1. National Jinan University

The school suffered considerable losses during the Shanghai war. After the war, it worked hard to reorganize, and is now gradually returning to its original state. It is organized into three colleges: Liberal Arts, Science, and Commerce, with fifteen departments. The administrative section has 115 staff members. The organization is considered too large, and the number of staff members is also considered excessive. The annual income is more than 697,000 yuan. After offsetting expenses, there is still a surplus. However, there are still more than 200,000 yuan in accumulated old and new debts. There are 143 faculty members, which is a slight increase compared to the previous inspection of full-time faculty, but is still considered insufficient. There are 872 students, with the College of Liberal Arts having the most. Military training and physical education are taken relatively seriously. However, the students' clothing is not plain, especially the female students. There are more than 50,000 books in the library, with some new additions in recent years. Scientific experiments are mostly improved in accordance with the Ministry's orders, and equipment has also increased slightly. The newly established printing house is performing well. Other sports and health equipment are quite sufficient.

2. Private Datong University

The school campus occupies 103 mu. The buildings are somewhat old, but still usable. A gymnasium and faculty residences have recently been added. A library and science hall are also planned for construction. There are 20 staff members, 22 full-time faculty members, and 13 part-time faculty members. There are 334 students. All students in each college are required to take mathematics, physics, and chemistry courses. The equipment in the College of Science is relatively complete. The school is managed economically and does not waste money. Faculty members are hardworking and dedicated. Students are simple and eager to learn. It is particularly valuable for teachers to guide students to conduct research independently. Last year's final budget showed an income of over 126,000 yuan, but expenses resulted in an annual deficit. The school is organized into three colleges: Liberal Arts, Science, and Commerce, with two attached specialized courses in English and mathematics. The duration of study and admission requirements for these courses do not meet the regulations. The curriculum arrangement is quite relevant. However, it is difficult to have university and middle school courses taught by the same professor at the same time. Students pay attention in class and have very few absences. All kinds of examinations are strictly administered. There are more than 24,000 books in the library. There are occasional feelings of lacking instruments, but overall, it is considered complete.

3. Private Hujiang University

The school campus occupies more than 300 mu. The buildings are complete and the environment is excellent. It is organized into four colleges: Liberal Arts, Science, Commerce, and Education, with a total of 14 departments. However, the names of some departments do not comply with the Ministry's regulations, and some departments have few students. The Department of Religion and Ethics does not have any specialized students. The annual income is more than 290,000 yuan. After offsetting income and expenses, there is still a surplus. The school's finances are absolutely transparent, and the budget is very stable, so there have been no deficits over the years. There are 45 staff members and 54 faculty members, all of whom are full-time. They are absolutely not allowed to hold part-time positions outside the school, and the school provides housing, so their lives are stable, they are diligent in their duties, and their spirit is extremely focused. There are 541 students. Discipline is good. Management is strict. Examinations are taken seriously. Extracurricular activities are also given great attention. However, everything at the school tends to be Europeanized, and students are accustomed to extravagance, especially female students. The Chinese language proficiency of first-year students is too poor, and even sentence construction is not fluent. This is because attention was not paid during enrollment. Books and instruments are quite complete, especially the equipment, talent, and teaching conditions of the College of Science, which are the best among the universities inspected. Sports, health, and other equipment are very complete and clean. The medical office is also well managed.

4. Private Fudan University

The school campus covers an area of 80 mu. The environment is very good. There are libraries, gymnasiums, health centers, and dormitories. A scientific laboratory is under construction. It is organized into four colleges: Liberal Arts, Science, Law, and Commerce, with 18 departments. There is also an attached normal school department. This is considered too large, and it is not easy to develop given the school's financial resources. Last year's final budget showed an income of over 1,189,000 yuan, but income and expenses could not be offset, resulting in continuous debt. There are 56 staff members, 17 full-time faculty members, and 79 part-time faculty members. Part-time faculty members account for about 80% of the total, which is far from the Ministry's prescribed ratio. There are 1,369 students. The Business School is developing well and is managed relatively successfully. The school's curriculum places too much emphasis on the credit system, so students' grades are often indistinguishable. The curriculum arrangement needs to be improved. Semester exams and school-wide final exams are relatively serious. Training and management are also strict. All first-year students live on campus and are given special training by designated teachers, which is especially appropriate. There is a lack of books, instruments, medicines, and equipment needed for various experiments. Other facilities, such as sports and health facilities, and the Business School's practical training facilities, are considered complete. In particular, the health center, a small-scale hospital, is managed even more successfully.

5. Private Guanghua University

The school campus covers an area of more than 100 mu. Libraries, science halls, gymnasiums, and auditoriums are still planned for construction. It is organized into three colleges: Liberal Arts, Science, and Commerce, with 13 departments. The annual income is 306,000 yuan, and the expenses are the same. However, there is a considerable amount of debt from the past. There are 29 staff members, most of whom are part-time. There are two vice-presidents, making it difficult to divide authority. Each college does not have a formal dean, but is instead headed by the department chair. Some deans hold administrative positions in other cities, or department chairs teach courses at other schools, or hold important positions at other schools. However, the school president has made considerable efforts to raise funds and maintain the school. Vice-President Zhu is also working hard. The registrar's office has a new and simple method for assessing student performance, and only two staff members are responsible for it, which is particularly economical. There are 60 faculty members, with full-time and part-time faculty members each accounting for half, which is not very appropriate. There are 689 students. Students in each college pay attention to basic subjects such as Chinese, foreign languages, and mathematics, which is quite appropriate. Faculty members mostly use English to teach. Examinations are not strict. The equipment in the Department of Physics in the College of Science is too simple, and the courses offered are not sufficient for major students. The equipment in the Department of Biology is sufficient for first-year students. Various books and equipment for basic science experiments are considered insufficient. Training and extracurricular activities are given attention. Students are mostly extravagant and Europeanized, especially female students' attire.

6. Private Daxia University

The school campus covers an area of 300 mu. The buildings are suitable and the environment is excellent. It is organized into five colleges: Liberal Arts, Science, Law, Commerce, and Education, with 15 departments. There is also an attached normal school specialized course, divided into four departments. The annual income is over 1,281,000 yuan. Income and expenses are currently balanced, but there is a considerable amount of debt from the past. The school has limited financial resources and too many departments, making it difficult to develop. The management of the Business School has not been successful. It is also inappropriate to have four departments in the normal school specialized course. There are 76 staff members and 76 faculty members, with too many part-time faculty members. There are 1,425 students. Classrooms are shared with the middle school, which is very insufficient. The cooperative spirit between faculty and students is very good. The College of Education is managed relatively well. The spirit of joint research between teachers and students is especially good. Training and management are considered serious. However, students' customs tend to be extravagant, and female students are even more frivolous. Chinese and Western books are not abundant. The lack of physical and chemical instruments and medicines is particularly serious. Sports and health equipment are sufficient.

In summary, the six schools inspected this time all have colleges of Liberal Arts, Science, and Commerce. Daxia and Fudan have colleges of Law, and Hujiang and Daxia have colleges of Education. Even if other schools do not have these colleges, they mostly have departments similar to these colleges. In Shanghai alone, there is such an overlap of university colleges and departments. It is impossible to seek overall development, whether in terms of economics or talent. Rather than having a large organization and engaging in extravagance without any development, it would be better to cut back and merge separately, reduce the scope, and seek special development. Therefore, the issue of colleges and departments in Shanghai universities really needs to be systematically reorganized by the government or by the schools themselves through voluntary joint efforts.

According to the current survey results, Datong and Hujiang Universities are the most dedicated to running schools. Hujiang and Datong Universities also manage the College of Science better. Daxia University manages the College of Education better, and Fudan University manages the Business School better. As for Guanghua University's recent reorganization and Jinan University's post-war reorganization, each has made considerable efforts. However, Guanghua University's administrative organization is not very sound, and the spirit is quite scattered.

The regular income of each school, except for Jinan, is at most just over 200,000 yuan per year, and at least only over 100,000 yuan. Given the specialization of university courses and the breadth of equipment, which require a lot of money, it is necessary to implement extremely economical methods in terms of expenses. The abuses of public schools, such as the misuse of staff and the waste of public funds, are rare in private schools. Except for Hujiang, all private schools are experiencing extremely difficult financial situations, but the school authorities do not slack off in their spirit, and even plan day and night to seek the development of school affairs. Their dedication to the cause and their hard work are admirable.

Except for Hujiang, each school has had deficits over the years, ranging from tens of thousands of yuan to two or three hundred thousand yuan. This is all due to insufficient funding. Due to insufficient funding, they often recruit more students and charge higher fees, and hire fewer full-time faculty members and pay lower salaries. Although each school plans to repay the deficits every year, it is ultimately futile. If this continues, it will be difficult to maintain. It is hoped that the central government can allocate some funds each year, select those with excellent performance, designate their use, and provide appropriate subsidies to show encouragement. Moreover, most of these private universities lack funds, and even if they do have them, the amount is very small. It is also hoped that each school will seek to remedy this on its own as soon as possible.

All faculty members at Hujiang are full-time. In other schools, part-time faculty members account for a large number. At Fudan, part-time faculty members account for 80%. According to the faculty rosters of each school, some teach at several schools, some serve as department chairs at two schools, and some even hold positions in other cities. Since their energy cannot be focused, teaching will naturally be inefficient. It is already insufficient to simply impart knowledge through lectures, let alone train talents and conduct research. If this is not improved, the impact on students' studies will be significant.

The enrollment issue is not very strict at most schools. This year, the percentage of applicants and those admitted at each school is slightly lower at Hujiang, and very high at the rest. It is even possible to enter university with a forged certificate after graduating from junior high school. If qualifications can be strictly reviewed and entrance exams can be seriously administered during enrollment, then these students will have no way to get by.

Most schools lack books and scientific experimental equipment. Many books are old or scattered and lack a system. There are limited new additions each year. The experimental equipment at Datong and Hujiang is sufficient and can be fully utilized, but it is still not complete. Jinan is still purchasing equipment due to the impact of the Shanghai war. The rest of the schools only have simple equipment for basic subjects. Even important courses that require experiments lack experimental equipment, so students have no practical experience.

Except for Hujiang, most schools' graduation theses are too narrow in scope. Some even plagiarize books and perfunctorily fulfill their responsibilities. Students do not actually benefit much. In the future, theses at each school should focus on practical research and explore specialized problems, so that students can gain practical experience and develop methods for independent research.

Among the schools' students, Datong's clothing is relatively plain. Most others are accustomed to extravagance and luxury, competing for novelty in clothing and shoes, and tending to be weak in physique. They even go to entertainment venues and are deeply influenced by current habits. This fact has been reported in newspapers many times. Female students' clothing is even more luxurious and novel. If this is not corrected, a simple and strong atmosphere will not be cultivated, and both families and society will suffer.

Regarding students' knowledge, during the inspection, representatives of the student self-government associations of one or two schools were selected for conversation, and asked what preparatory work students should do during the national crisis. They were also asked for their opinions on national higher education policies and the specific plans of the self-government association to lead students. The students were unable to answer. After a long time, they began to express their opinions, but they were mostly empty, superficial, and impractical. Each school should pay special attention to the educational work of clarifying shame and fighting the war, and reviving the nation, so as not to betray the fundamental purpose of university education.

Educational Development in Shanxi Province 201

Compulsory education is most universal

Normal school students receive special treatment

There are scholarships for entering middle school and university

| Remarks after inspection by Supervisor Gu of the Ministry of Education |

After Gu Zhaoluo, supervisor of the Ministry of Education, returned to the ministry after inspecting education in Shanxi and other provinces, he said that Shanxi's methods for popularizing compulsory education are cost-effective and have significant results, and other provinces and cities can follow them by law. He also talked about several special features of education at all levels, which are described separately below.

▲Compulsory Education　Shanxi Province is the most developed and universal province in terms of compulsory education for elementary schools. When Director Ji of the Shanxi Provincial Department of Education took office in the 21st year of the Republic [1932], there were 5,000 out-of-school children in the provincial capital. Now there are only more than 1,000 out-of-school children. Not only is this the case in Taiyuan City, but in rural elementary schools such as Dai County, there are now only more than 100 out-of-school children. These more than 100 people, and the more than 1,000 people in Taiyuan, are all because the students' families are too poor and need to find other ways to help. Generally, ordinary families can go to school. The reasons are: (1) elementary schools do not charge tuition fees; (2) they do not charge accommodation fees; (3) meal fees are very low, only about one yuan and a few cents per month. A student who receives a complete elementary school education only needs to pay a total of about 20 yuan per year, including meals, accommodation, books, and supplies. Moreover, the village administration in the province is very well managed. There is a system from top to bottom, which also provides a lot of assistance for the popularization of compulsory education. Director Ji of the Department of Education also set up five experimental elementary schools. The experimental schools are divided into three systems: (1) regular classes; (2) short-term classes; (3) simplified classes. This adjustment also makes it easier to promote compulsory education. Generally, society is skeptical of short-term and simplified classes. Since a school has three systems, students with poor qualifications can enter short-term or simplified classes, and outstanding students can be promoted to regular classes. Teaching students according to their aptitude can dispel society's doubts and fulfill their wishes. This method can be followed by various provinces.

▲Secondary Education　(1) The province originally had six normal school districts. The most peculiar thing is that the classes in the normal schools outside the provincial capital are not connected, especially for female normal schools. The Department of Education plans to merge the first three years of normal school into middle school to run the first three years of general middle school, and set up separate normal schools for the last three years. (2) The funding for middle schools, except for Taiyuan City, is relatively abundant. The funding for middle schools outside the province does not have a fixed standard, especially for girls' schools. The Department of Education is drafting a draft funding standard, which has not yet been finalized. It is expected that next year, there will be a standard for middle school funding to follow. (3) There are no senior high schools for girls. Except for a few private senior high schools that occasionally admit girls, there are no senior high schools for girls inside or outside the province, so girls have fewer opportunities for further education. This year, the Department of Education took over the private Guanghua Girls' Middle School and renamed it the Provincial Taiyuan Girls' Junior Middle School. In the future, it plans to add a senior high school to enable girls' education to be further developed. (4) The most special phenomenon in the province is that girls' education is not developed. There is one girls' middle school and five girls' normal schools in the province, and the number of students is not large. In the girls' normal school classes, the class with the fewest students has only six to eight students per grade. The social psychology of the province generally does not want girls to go to school more. According to this situation, in the future, the province may reduce the number of girls' normal schools and add girls' normal school classes in boys' normal schools to save money.

▲Higher Education　(1) Shanxi University in the province was established during the Guangxu period [1875-1908]. It has the longest history and is similar to Beiyang University. It has three colleges: Liberal Arts, Law, and Engineering. The annual expenditure is 272,314 yuan, which is currently paid at 80%. The school was national during the former Beijing Ministry of Education era. After the establishment of the National Government, the Ministry of Education ordered it to be changed to provincial. However, the general faculty and students are still seeking to restore the national movement. The reason they hold is that the central and local taxes are not clearly divided. Part of the funding is provided by the province, and part is paid by the national treasury. There are currently 700 male and female students. The affiliated high school also has several hundred students. Previously, the Ministry of Education ordered the merger of the private Law and Education colleges due to the duplication of departments. The reason why they have not been merged to this day is that the funding standards are different, and it is not easy for the province to raise additional funds (420,000 yuan after the merger). Also, the faculty and students of Shanxi University, in order to seek the restoration of the national movement, believe that merging the private Law and Education colleges and proceeding with nationalization would be inconvenient, so they are not enthusiastic about the merger. The school spent a lot of money when it was established, so the campus and equipment are quite impressive. However, the annual fee is only more than 20,000 yuan per month, and it must be paid at 80%. Since it includes three colleges, the recent equipment has not increased significantly. The College of Engineering has departments of machinery, electrical engineering, and civil engineering. President Wang is a specialized scholar, so graduates of the College of Engineering have made considerable achievements in serving the province (such as the design and construction of provincial roads by graduates of the College of Engineering). The library equipment of the Colleges of Liberal Arts and Law and the existing classics are sufficient for use, but the reference books for application need to be expanded. (2) The Industrial Specialized School merged the Industrial Experimental Institute and the Model Factory into the school when Xishan retired in the 20th year of the Republic [1931], so the machinery is better equipped. The production of magnetic and kiln smelting can produce high-temperature flasks, and the results are good. There is also machine leather production, and the products are of good quality. However, due to the lack of marketing methods, it has not been possible to sell them for maximum profit. (3) The Commercial Specialized School and the Agricultural Specialized School are generally well managed, but the equipment is slightly lacking. (4) The private Bingzhou College has departments of Liberal Arts and Law, and more than 400 students. This year, a Department of Chemistry was established, and it is initially able to follow the central government's approach to focusing on science. Although it was registered during the former Beijing Ministry of Education era, it has not gone through the registration procedures in modern times. (5) The private Chuanzhi Medical Specialized School has good equipment, and President Jin is also able to work hard. The affiliated midwifery department is very successful. Most of its graduates serve as military doctors, and few practice medicine privately.

Vocational Education　Vocational education in the province has been unsuccessful because the A and B vocational industrial and commercial schools that were previously run were not effective, and there was no way out after graduation. Society is very skeptical of vocational education, and the plans formulated by educational administration have not taken vocational education into account, so it has not been established. After discussing the situation with the Ministry of Education supervisor, the most important principles were determined as follows: (1) Promote vocational education. Without increasing education fees, by the 26th year of the Republic [1937], vocational education funding will account for 35% of secondary education funding standards. (2) According to Yan Xishan's ten-year construction plan, there are local special products (such as animal husbandry, salt affairs, etc.), but new-style industries and the manufacture of products are insufficient, whether manual or mechanical, resulting in little success in management. It is necessary to find ways to improve them. It is also important to cultivate students' technical skills and work habits. After discussion, the education community in the province has gained the courage to try. According to Shanxi's production situation, the new industries in the future will be centered on Taiyuan, because the original arsenal and paper mill are concentrated in Taiyuan. If a vocational industrial school is set up here, there will be no shortage of students, and it can be distributed throughout the province, and the so-called special production can be carried out in parallel. Special production will be centered on the local area. (3) The establishment of departments and methods for vocational schools in the future, as well as the issue of teachers, has been generally discussed, but has not yet been decided. According to Shanxi's lack of junior technical talents, it is necessary to widely establish vocational supplementary schools in the future, followed by junior vocational schools. It is not necessary to establish many senior vocational schools, but the teachers of vocational schools are very important. If technical teachers can be carefully trained, it seems better than training many normal school students who explore academic theories.

▲Scholarship Methods　Those who enter normal school in the province, whether it is the pre-term general science or the post-term normal science, receive a meal subsidy of five yuan per month. Students actually eat for two yuan and a few cents, and the remaining two yuan and a few cents per month can be used to purchase school supplies. This is the preferential treatment for normal school. Those in ordinary middle schools and universities have scholarships. Each county has a sum of money set aside for students from the county to go to school. Counties with good results (that is, fewer students going to school can be allocated more) can receive a subsidy of 70 to 80 yuan per person per year. Counties with poor results can also be divided into 30 to 40 yuan. This refers to going to middle school in the province. If they go to specialized schools or higher outside the province, they can receive a subsidy of 70 to 80 yuan from the county at the same time, and a subsidy of more than 100 yuan from the province. Therefore, those who go to school outside the province pay very little private money themselves. This scholarship method can be said to be uniquely excellent. However, because the departments in higher education in the province are duplicated, those who go to school in Beiping mostly enter departments of Liberal Arts and Law, and only one in ten enters science and engineering departments, which is due to their usual teaching. This is the whole problem of Shanxi education. After this inspection by the Ministry of Education supervisor, the Department of Education also knows that there is a bias in the education of the whole province, and will have new plans to reorganize it.

The Third County National Products Exhibition Entry Deadline Today 204

▲ And Opening the First Exhibit Review Meeting

▲ Preferential Transportation for Exhibits on the Shanghai-Minhang Route

The third Shanghai County National Products Movement Exhibition is scheduled to open on New Year's Day next year in Beiqiao. Preparations are currently underway. The national products sales area is located at the site of the bell tower of Mingxin Temple. A tent is currently being added. Details are as follows:

Entry Deadline and Start of Review 205

Since the exhibition began accepting entries on the 10th of this month, progress has been smooth. Manufacturers from various industries in Shanghai are enthusiastically participating due to the location being a major transportation hub between Shanghai and Hangzhou. As of yesterday, more than 200 manufacturers have participated in the display, with 2,000 exhibits. Local specialties from various counties account for more than half of the exhibits. The entry deadline is today, and the first Exhibit Review Committee meeting will be held at 5:00 PM this afternoon to begin reviewing the exhibits.

Preferential Transportation Measures for Exhibits 206

To facilitate the transportation of exhibits for exhibitors, the exhibition has specially appointed Zhang Yi and others to negotiate with the Shanghai-Minhang, Shanghai-Songjiang, and Shanghai-Nanhui long-distance bus companies to establish the following preferential measures: (1) Holders of certificates from this county can ride Shanghai-Minhang, Shanghai-Songjiang, and Shanghai-Nanhui buses at half price; (2) Holders of certificates from this exhibition can transport exhibits using their own vehicles without paying road tolls; (3) Holders of certificates from this exhibition can transport exhibits on Shanghai-Minhang, Shanghai-Songjiang, and Shanghai-Nanhui buses at baggage rates.

The Third Public Education Film Show of the Education Film Association Branch 207

▲ Held Yesterday at the Lake Society and the People's Education Center

▲ Approximately Over One Thousand Attendees at Both Venues

The Shanghai branch of the China Educational Film Association, in order to promote educational films to people from all walks of life, in addition to regularly screening films in schools and various factories, shops, and organizations, holds two public educational film festivals every month for public viewing. The Southern District held two screenings at the Municipal Public Education Center. Yesterday was the third. The Central District held its first screening yesterday at the Lake Society. From 9:00 AM to 11:30 AM, two shows were screened at each venue. A total of more than one thousand viewers attended. In addition to screening educational films with simple explanations, the association also screened comedic films to increase interest. Therefore, the audience was very willing to attend. The association is currently planning to hold public education film festivals once a week, starting next year, simultaneously in the east, south, west, north, and central districts to show its wide reach.

Foot Fungus Problems 229

— Pang Jingzhou

Foot fungus is a common ailment among people in southern China. It manifests as intense itching between the toes, white maceration, peeling skin, small blisters, oozing yellow fluid, and a foul odor. In some cases, it can even spread to the dorsum and sole of the foot, leading to ulceration and difficulty in walking. Because it feels more comfortable after the fluid is released, it is commonly referred to as "dampness." The small holes that appear in the dermis during the initial peeling stage of the blisters are why it is also called "foot rot."

According to traditional medical theory, this is a way for "dampness" to exit the body. Having it means you won't develop a more serious illness. Patients themselves often say it's one of life's great pleasures. In the mild to moderate stages, soaking the feet in hot water every night feels very comfortable. Or, having a pedicurist scrape the affected area with a metal blade every few days, scraping until blood comes out and the itching stops, can also create a feeling of complete relaxation.

However, in our view, even if "dampness" is a euphemism for some kind of disease, the body already has sweat pores, the bowels, and the urinary tract as excretory mechanisms for releasing dampness. To deliberately create a blood-soaked path on healthy skin for the smooth flow of dampness hardly seems to be the intention of nature in creating humans. Furthermore, people in the north rarely suffer from foot fungus. Does this mean they don't need to release dampness? Why is it that southerners, who sacrifice their flesh and blood to release so much dampness, are still prone to contracting damp-heat illnesses that northerners don't? How can this be explained? The fact is that medical experts haven't recognized what foot fungus really is, nor do they know how to guide the "dampness" released from the feet to the proper channels of urination, defecation, or sweat pores for excretion. Thus, they have concocted a specious theory that has deeply poisoned people's minds. Initially, people even harbor the disease, thinking it beneficial, a clear case of mistaking a thief for a father. Later, seeking relief from the itching, they resort to hot water and metal blades, unknowingly forming a habit. This then turns into a fondness for crusts, like the untalented eccentric Jin Shengtan, who said, "Leaving one or two sores on the private parts to scratch in secret is a great pleasure." Who would have thought that, three hundred years later, his followers haven't diminished in number. But think about it, everyone, is there any difference between scratching sores on one's private parts in secret and a beggar delousing himself in the sun? Why must civilized people seek pleasure in such a state?

An investigation reveals that foot fungus is a skin disease caused by a parasitic organism, specifically a type of fungus. These fungi are commonly found in the air. If they attach to human skin and the environment is suitable, they will develop, grow, and cause disease. (For example, people with sweaty feet are prone to developing it between their toes because the environment is suitable for the fungus.) It can spread from the toes to the hands, causing similar symptoms. This fungus is not unique to China, but it is more prevalent in southern China and warmer regions, such as Southeast Asia and Hong Kong. Foreigners in Hong Kong first discovered this condition, and therefore they named it "Hong Kong foot." It is less common in colder regions because the climate is not conducive to the fungus. The fungus dies off, and the disease cures itself. To put it simply, foot fungus is a type of "tropical infectious skin disease."

I myself have suffered from this disease and have been cured. It has recurred, and I have cured it again. (Actually, it wasn't a recurrence, but rather a re-infection. These things are common in the air, and they often lurk inside old shoes. If you suddenly wear shoes that haven't been worn for a long time and you happen to sweat a lot, it can happen again. But as long as you wash your feet diligently after being cured, it's unlikely to return.) I feel that after this disease was eradicated, I did not develop any other ailments. There was truly no difference. Moreover, I have cured countless others. I believe that a compound ointment I concocted based on the cause of the disease is very effective. Those who have been cured have also reported to me that "there's no difference." Among them, a few honestly said, "Because the itching between my toes has suddenly stopped, I feel a bit unaccustomed for a short period of time. But I haven't developed any other serious illnesses."

However, those who advocate the theory of "dampness exit" have one compelling piece of evidence: "Whenever someone with foot fungus suddenly stops oozing fluid, they often develop a fever or become ill, or even become seriously ill and bedridden, and the foot fungus actually improves. These are all undeniable facts." However, this is a case of reversed causality. It is because a person is about to become ill that the foot fungus stops oozing fluid, due to changes in the skin's resistance to the fungus. When a person is already ill, it stops oozing even more, for the same reason. As for being bedridden for a long time, naturally one is lying flat and barefoot, without the constraints of shoes and socks, and without sticky foot sweat. The toes are ventilated and dry, which is most unfavorable for the propagation of this fungus. Just look at farmers who often work barefoot in the fields. They are exposed to a lot of dampness, yet they don't develop foot fungus. Consider friends who wear sandals in the summer. Their foot fungus can also cure itself. Doesn't this disprove the theory of "dampness exit"? There is no shortage of bold individuals in society. Please try curing your foot fungus and see if you develop any serious illnesses. Then the truth of medicine will be clear.

Discussing the Effect of "Day and Night" on Human Physiological Functions 230

— Zhu Yanggao

Doctors in the past did not conduct much research on this aspect because scientific knowledge about the specifics of natural cycles was limited. In recent years, however, significant progress in climatology has gradually clarified the relationship between medicine and this issue. In reality, common folk experience has already proven certain facts, such as the influence of weather on temperament and general ailments. However, these observations could not be explained using scientific methods. These phenomena are abundant not only among the Chinese populace but also among various ethnic groups worldwide.

In the natural world, apart from humans, we have long recognized such relationships. For example, certain plant blossoms only open at night (night-blooming jasmine), while others close at night. The French botanist Lmno called this phenomenon the sleep of flowers, stating that we can use this phenomenon to observe time, making it a "floral clock." Its accuracy is evident. Our common people also know of such phenomena, such as recognizing the start of spring when plum blossoms bloom. These instances prove the relationship between the life activities of plants and the cycles of nature. Their actions change accordingly. Germans call it Kosmische BceuiＩussg auf des Lebeu. In the animal kingdom, we know that the physiological functions of many animals have an inseparable connection with the lunar cycle. In the ocean depths, there is a type of spiny-haired worm whose mating season invariably coincides with a fixed period of lunar change, without deviation (the specific period is unknown to the reporter at the moment). In short, we can point out close relationships in both the plant and animal kingdoms. It is not surprising to find similar phenomena in humans.

Human physiological functions also exhibit this type of phenomenon. For example, we desire to be awake during the day and to sleep at night; to be active when awake and to rest when asleep. This is a natural cycle. According to Eores, humans are awake during the day and asleep at night because the visual organs are the primary organs, so they must be awake when stimulated by sunlight and sleep during darkness. Birds, whose primary organs are also their eyes, also share the same sleep-wake cycle as humans. Animals like dogs differ from humans because their primary organ is their sense of smell. These facts are apparent to everyone. Although we have electric lights and other industrial inventions that provide light, working at night is never as enjoyable as working during the day, and one always feels more fatigued in the evening. Some who work at night have conducted experiments, letting themselves wake and sleep at will during the day. But even after long-term trials, they could not achieve the same joy and lightness of working during the day. Therefore, the reason for sleeping and waking lies in the distinction between day and night, and not entirely in daytime overexertion that necessitates nighttime rest.

Besides the sleep-wake cycle, there are other cyclical physiological functions, such as the fall of blood pressure, stimulation of the respiratory center, decline in libido, and decrease in heart rate. The acidity in the blood increases in quantity due to respiration. The excretion of phosphorus compounds in the urine also increases accordingly. All of these are closely related to nighttime sleep. Moreover, temperature changes also follow a cyclical pattern. Old theories often attributed the rise in temperature at dusk solely to the impact of daytime work. However, this notion can no longer be sustained. Experiments conducted with long-term (eight-year) night workers explain that the rise and fall in temperature is a natural response, following a cycle, and cannot be entirely eliminated by other actions. Similar to this temperature cycle are the excretion of urine volume (the lowest volume at 12:00 AM, the highest in the forenoon) and the discharge of liver and gallbladder glycogen.

Besides the various physiological functions mentioned above, there are certainly other, as-yet-unexplained examples. Human physiology functions in accordance with the ideal of Reaksfoneu u·Gegenreaksicnen (reaction and counter-reaction). So, there might not be a single human physiological activity that isn't closely related to day and night. The ultimate control of various cycles, of course, resides in the brain, especially the Hypophysen Lwischenhirnsyssem (midbrain system). There is clinical evidence to support this assertion. Nevertheless, there is a specific region in the human body responsible for controlling such cycles. However, we must also consider whether this discovered function originates internally or is stimulated by external factors. The latter explanation is feasible. We can use animal experiments to prove that the root cause lies entirely in the effects of "sunlight" and "darkness." These two conditions are the driving force behind this cyclical pattern. In reality, we must consider that day and night do not fundamentally occur simultaneously at all points on Earth. And when people reach nighttime in their respective locations, they all exhibit the phenomenon of fatigue. Is this not a clear piece of evidence?

Common Knowledge Questions and Answers About Diseases 231

— Cheng Hanzhang

(22) Pleurisy

(Q) What part of the body does pleurisy affect?

(A) Pleurisy is one of the most common diseases of the respiratory system. It is an inflammation of the pleura, which covers the outside of the lungs and the inside of the chest cavity.

(Q) What are the causes of pleurisy?

(A) There are many causes: some are primary, such as colds or injuries. Others are secondary, often following tuberculosis, pneumonia, rheumatic arthritis, peritonitis, pericarditis, and various infectious diseases.

(Q) What are the general symptoms?

(A) It often starts with mild chills and fever. Pain develops in the chest on the affected side, radiating from the affected area towards the side of the chest, the back, or the abdomen. Frequent coughing occurs, but without phlegm. The patient's pulse rate increases, the complexion becomes pale, the body feels tired, and the appetite decreases.

Page 14

(Q) What are the different types of pleurisy?

(A) There are dry, wet, and purulent types.

(Q) What is dry pleurisy like?

(A) In dry pleurisy, breathing movements are limited on the affected side of the chest. Percussion produces a high-pitched sound, and auscultation reveals friction rubs. The patient prefers to lie on the healthy side. If the inflamed area is near the diaphragm, percussion may not reveal friction rubs, but there will be pain in the hypochondriac region, which intensifies when swallowing.

(Q) What is wet pleurisy like?

(A) Wet pleurisy involves a large amount of effusion, causing the affected area to swell. Breathing is uneven on both sides. The apex beat of the heart is compressed and shifts towards the healthy side. The position of the liver and spleen is also affected. The patient often lies on the affected side. Percussion produces a dull sound in the affected area, with a slightly tympanic sound above the dullness. As the effusion decreases, auscultation reveals friction rubs on the upper border of the dullness. Fever fluctuates with the amount of effusion. The amount of urine also decreases. As the effusion is absorbed, urination increases.

(Q) What is purulent pleurisy like?

(A) When pyogenic bacteria invade and cause pleurisy, the effusion becomes purulent. This is purulent pleurisy. The patient often develops a high fever accompanied by intermittent chills, fatigue, headache, and rapid pulse. Chest pain is severe. Because adhesions of the pleura are rare, bronchial sounds can often be heard.

(Q) What is the prognosis of pleurisy and how dangerous is it?

(A) Dry pleurisy is usually not dangerous, but it often leads to pulmonary tuberculosis. Wet pleurisy depends on the amount of effusion and the age of the patient. Most cases are tubercular and cannot be completely cured. A large amount of effusion can be life-threatening.

(Q) What are the dangers if the effusion is not absorbed?

(A) If the effusion remains for a long time, it will form a hardening, causing adhesions of the pleura, leading to atrophy. If the atrophy is extensive, the chest wall will become flattened, and the spine will curve towards the affected side.

(Q) What diseases can develop after exudative pleurisy?

(A) Chronic bronchitis, bronchiectasis, and thoracic neuralgia can develop.

(Q) What are the treatments for pleurisy?

(A) Complete bed rest is essential. It is important to pay attention to cardiac function and administer cardiotonic drugs. If coughing is severe, narcotics such as codeine can be given. For fever, antipyretics are used. For pain, local application of warm cloths or poultices is used. For rheumatic pleurisy, salicylates can be administered internally. For chronic pleurisy, iodides are used. Diuretics are used to promote the drainage of effusion, or thoracentesis is performed to aspirate the retained fluid. However, thoracentesis is contraindicated in hemorrhagic pleurisy. When there is pus in the chest cavity, thoracotomy is necessary.

How to Enhance Our Health and Longevity 232

— Guo Renji

If we can strive for hygiene and physical fitness in our daily lives, we can achieve strength and health. As a result of health, we will inevitably attain longevity.

Do those who hear this doubt my words? Those who have trained their physique have stronger bodily functions than the average person. Therefore, their resistance to disease is stronger, and their ability to recover is also stronger. Unless the invasion of an external disease is overwhelmingly powerful, they will not fall ill. Even if they do fall ill, those who die are few, and they will recover quickly.

Suppose two individuals suffer the same injury. If one is an athlete, they will heal quickly and without a trace. If one is elderly or weak, granulation tissue will not form easily, healing will be slow, and suppuration is likely to occur. The wound will not heal easily, especially in cases of tuberculosis. The resulting scar will also be unsightly.

There are also cases of injury or disease without presenting symptoms. Mr. Pettenkofer once swallowed a pure culture of Vibrio cholerae, conducting his famous self-experiment. Because of his strong digestive function, even with concentrated Vibrio cholerae in his intestines, he proved that it would not trigger cholera (severe cholera).

It is not uncommon for acute infectious diseases such as typhoid fever or influenza to spread within a family, and yet one person remains unaffected. That person is usually someone who is fully healthy and very active. This is a common experience.

The above are all examples of the body's ability to overcome disease. Unfortunately, a very virulent pathogen may invade, and even the strongest person may not be able to resist and will die prematurely. Therefore, if we wish to achieve longevity, we must strive for hygiene and physical fitness in our daily lives. We must improve all bodily functions and become strong to broaden the scope of our lives.

Looking at the statistics on mortality and causes of death reported by various civilized nations in the East and West, the largest causes of death among humans, besides infectious and digestive diseases, are diseases of the respiratory and circulatory systems, accounting for about a quarter of all deaths. However, these organ systems can generally be strengthened through hygiene and exercise. Therefore, those who focus on physical education and have strengthened these functions are not as afraid of these diseases.

However, gastrointestinal diseases account for more than 15% of deaths. In the past, some argued that athletes had shorter lifespans, which warrants attention. However, this argument was based on observations of martial arts athletes. The training methods of athletes in that transitional era were not yet standardized, and they did not know about hygiene. Occasionally, some of them died prematurely in succession, leading to alarming pronouncements to attract attention. It is known that when they were in their youth, they often overindulged in food and drink, and their training was irregular or overly intense. During competitions, they relied on their natural physical strength, thinking it would last forever. During this period of vigorous physical activity, they could easily digest large amounts of food and did not show symptoms from excessive drinking. However, when they gradually retired from the athletic world, they did not change their bad habits and continued to overeat and drink excessively, while exercise had stopped. As a result, they succumbed to disease and died prematurely. This is a common occurrence.

However, this does not happen to today's scientific athletes. They never overeat and strictly adhere to a very regular lifestyle. They understand that failing to observe hygiene and neglecting training will ultimately prevent them from achieving good results. They constantly strive to strengthen their bodies and maintain their health. Therefore, sports figures in the East and West have never suffered from such calamities.

We practice strengthening methods, continue to maintain our strength and health, and eventually achieve a natural death, which is to die of old age. This is called longevity. Unnatural death is called premature death. Among unnatural deaths, some are suicide, poisoning, or injuries that suddenly attack the body. Most diseases can only invade the body when our health is reduced or when we are in an unhealthy state. A person in perfect health will not fall ill unless their health is first impaired. It is as if there is a barrier or trench between them and disease, acting as a defense.

There are various causes of unnatural death. Some originate internally:

Heredity. Mental derangement. Functional derangement. Other unknown causes.

Some originate externally:

Temperature. Humidity. Poisoning. Trauma. Fungi. Parasites.

There are also other unknown factors.

These causes may be singular or multiple, internal and external factors interacting, or death may be caused by only one factor. The time between the appearance of the cause of death and death itself is called Necrobiose "indirect tissue death." The duration varies. In the case of trauma, it may take only a few seconds. In the case of chronic infections, it may last for decades.

During this time, our body vigorously activates various functions to defend against or expel diseases. Lymph and white blood cells actively circulate. Blood serum swirls. The liver performs its functions. Endocrine glands increase their activity. As a result, phenomena such as redness, swelling, suppuration, fever, sweating, and secretions manifest.

If these resistance and defense mechanisms are successful, Necrobiose will cease, and the individual will return to their previous state of health. These defensive and resistant functions are even stronger in generally strong and healthy people.

The outside of our body is completely covered by skin or mucous membranes. If a person is in perfect health, there are no cracks in the body's surface, and pathogens cannot invade. It is as if these external enemies are all repelled beyond the borders. However, it is difficult for the body's surface to be completely free of cracks. Therefore, external enemies can easily enter the country and disrupt peace. However, pathogens generally lack the ability to move on their own. Some are completely unable to move without assistance. If we do not deliberately open the door and invite them in, they will not be able to invade. Those who are good at nurturing life should pay close attention to this.

Introducing a Famous Book

An Overview of Medicine and Pharmaceuticals in Shanghai over the Past Decade 233

This book is written by Dr. Pang Jingzhou. It was serialized in the Medical and Pharmaceutical Weekly of the Shen Bao newspaper. Now it has been revised and compiled, with the addition of several detailed statistical tables, and published as a separate volume. The contents are divided into seven chapters and twenty-one sections, describing in detail all aspects of the medical and pharmaceutical industries in Shanghai. It is an essential read for those interested in the modern medicine and pharmaceutical industry and those within the industry itself. This book will be published next January and sells for only 40 cents per copy.

Available at the Science Company on Foch Road, the Shen Bao newspaper office, the Shanghai Medical Association, the Medical and Pharmaceutical Review Society, Wuding Company, Dr. Pang's Clinic, and the Social Medical Journal, among other places.
