Economic Supplement

The Four Stages of Improving Chinese Bookkeeping 234

— Xu Yongzuo

Although I (the author, referring to myself) studied accounting bookkeeping in school, my focused research began after 1919 or 1920. At that time, I was the chief editor of the "Banking Weekly." To facilitate discussion among enthusiasts, I started a "Accounting Research" column in the newspaper, briefly outlining my views. During this period, my research focused entirely on Western double-entry bookkeeping, and I advocated it with unwavering conviction. I believed that Chinese accounting books were upside down, chaotic, fragmented, and of no research value. I advocated complete abandonment and adoption of Western horizontal-style bookkeeping. When planning accounting systems for various companies, I also followed this approach, as exemplified by the accounting books for the stock exchange. This was the first stage of my efforts to improve Chinese bookkeeping. My advocacy was purely for Western double-entry bookkeeping, and my implementations were all in large-scale modern enterprises. I had no accurate understanding of Chinese bookkeeping and was no different from the general proponents of Western bookkeeping today.

Around 1932, having practiced as a certified public accountant for several years, and realizing that Western bookkeeping was not easily understood by the general public and that complete imitation was inconvenient, I considered the following: Firstly, switching to Western bookkeeping meant relying on imported supplies, which were expensive and difficult to procure, making it an undesirable improvement strategy. Secondly, when submitting an audit report to the court for a certain case, the judge requested a separate report because he was unfamiliar with Arabic numerals. This showed that adopting Western bookkeeping had its obstacles. However, I was still reluctant to abandon Western bookkeeping, so I made slight modifications to the format, such as changing horizontal writing to vertical, using Chinese characters for all records, and listing amounts in Chinese characters while omitting place names between each number, such as tens, hundreds, thousands, etc., using lines or dots to separate the place values. I used domestic paper for the accounting books and a brush for recording. I subsequently planned accounting organizations for a certain chamber of commerce and two universities, based on this approach. Those who used it found it convenient. When planning the accounting organization for a certain chamber of commerce, I originally intended to have both horizontal and vertical styles, but the vertical style was ultimately adopted for its convenience. However, the accounting principles and methods were all based on the Western style, which was not easily learned by the general public. The numbers were written neatly within grids, which was not conducive to quick writing. The accounting books required a specific format and special printing, which was difficult to replenish. All these factors hindered its promotion in commerce and industry. This was the second stage of my efforts to improve Chinese bookkeeping. Even today, many government accounting systems still use this method for improvement. However, at this stage, I only maintained the form of Chinese bookkeeping, while still leaning heavily towards Western bookkeeping in terms of content.

In 1925 and 1926, realizing that it was difficult to promote Western-style bookkeeping in China, and that the improvement plan of maintaining the form of Chinese bookkeeping also had many obstacles, I had more contact with the commercial and industrial sectors due to my professional work. At the same time, I worked hard on the investigation and research of Chinese bookkeeping, and gained some insights, which changed my concept of Chinese bookkeeping. I believed that Chinese bookkeeping was not without organization, and that the accounting method was not entirely unreasonable. The problem was the inconsistency. Not only was it necessary to maintain it in form, but it also had its value in essence. And given its wide use and long history, I felt that the foundation was very strong and could not be replaced by Western bookkeeping. But at the same time, I also found that it had many shortcomings and needed to be improved. At that time, I planned the accounting organization for various companies based on this view, stipulating the classification of accounts, the organization of accounting books, and accounting rules, etc., so that the handling of accounting affairs had a certain standard. The pure cash accounting method (that is, the running entry is copied and cleaned, and the receipts and payments are not reversed) that has been used in China for a long time was used as before. The use of full writing or numerical characters for the amount was left to the freedom of the bookkeeper. The accounting books were not specially printed in a fixed format in order to facilitate implementation. This was the third stage of my efforts to improve Chinese bookkeeping. The results have been good so far. However, the common regret at that time was that the amount occupied more space, the accounting books were in vertical style, and the multi-column accounting method could not be adopted. The control accounting method, which is most commendable in Western bookkeeping, could not be imitated. Therefore, it was considered that improving Chinese bookkeeping was only suitable for those with fewer receipts and payments, and was not enough to talk about large-scale enterprises. In 1926 and 1927, I gave a speech at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, and mentioned this as a shortcoming. Today's reformers of Chinese bookkeeping still have this feeling.

In recent years, I have been entrusted to design improved Chinese bookkeeping for the business community more and more, and the results have gradually become apparent. And there has been continuous progress in the understanding of Chinese bookkeeping and the discovery of improvement methods. The most gratifying things are the following three:

(1) The ability of Western bookkeeping methods to adapt the organization of accounting books to the size of the business and the complexity of the accounts is entirely dependent on the use of multi-column accounting methods and the division of accounting books to achieve differentiation and aggregation, and to improve the efficiency of accounting work. Chinese accounting books are written vertically, and the vertical width should not be too long. Although there is no convenience for laying out multiple columns of amounts, the method of dividing accounting books can be used to change the organization of accounting books. For example, cash diaries can be divided into several books, such as cash diaries, bank diaries, incoming bill diaries, outgoing bill diaries, and transfer diaries, based on the purpose of receipts and payments. If the nature of the accounts is the standard, it can be divided into several books, such as purchase payment, sales receipt, various expenses, and cash diaries. In addition, such as goods books, cleaning books, etc., can be divided into several types according to their nature, this is one of them. (2) In Western bookkeeping, there is the so-called voucher bookkeeping method, which uses vouchers instead of accounting books. There is also the so-called control bookkeeping method, which summarizes and records similar items in order to facilitate posting and settlement. Both save a great deal of labor and expense in accounting affairs. Because of handling the accounting affairs of a certain cardboard company and a certain shipping company (both using Western voucher bookkeeping methods), I discovered a simple control bookkeeping method in Chinese bookkeeping, which was implemented in a certain pharmacy and a certain bookstore, and achieved great results, this is the second thing.

(3) The four-column clearing register is an ancient method in our country. If it can be used well, it can be used to compile daily, monthly or annual settlement statements based on various differentiated diaries and cleaning books. It can check whether there are any errors in recording and calculation in each period; and it can show the results and processes of account receipts and payments in each period, and compare them. Compared with the balance trial calculation method of Western bookkeeping, the effect is even greater, this is the third thing. With these three new discoveries, Chinese bookkeeping can also be applied to the accounting of large-scale enterprises, such as a large tobacco company, a large pharmacy, a large bookstore, etc., which are typical examples. Improving Chinese bookkeeping can be said to have a rough outline. Since last year, I have decided to formulate a standard plan to seek universal improvement of Chinese bookkeeping, but I have not been able to do so in a hurry. In May and June this year, I was invited by the Accounting and Political Society to lecture in Nanjing. Most of the listeners were accounting scholars, and some also involved this issue, all of whom were appreciated. But vulgar affairs are bleak, and it has been a long time without success. Since October, I have abandoned all affairs and devoted myself to this. Then I wrote a book called "An Overview of Improving Chinese Bookkeeping," which is divided into six chapters: Introduction, Improvement Outline, Account Classification, Accounting Book Organization, Accounting Book Formats, and Registration Methods, and Accounting Rules, etc., to be published and asked for correction from colleagues. This is the fourth stage of my efforts to improve Chinese bookkeeping.

This improvement plan is considered to be a reasonable bookkeeping method. In China, it can also be used as a standard for bookkeeping methods. Compared with Western double-entry bookkeeping, there is nothing that cannot be connected in principle. As for the accounting books being vertical, the accounting method being separate receipts and payments, the writing being in Chinese, and the paper being domestic products, although it is convenient for promotion, it has never deviated from the principles of double-entry bookkeeping. If I have time in the future, I plan to compile a bookkeeping book with Chinese and Western styles listed side by side, which may also be for the self-promotion of Chinese bookkeeping methods.

All of the above are the author's experiences over the years. In the future, I also plan to give public lectures in various universities, publish special issues in the accounting magazine published by my office, and add special courses to the affiliated training classes to promote the development of the Chinese bookkeeping improvement movement. I hope that accounting experts at home and abroad will come forward to teach me.

The Significance of Improving Chinese Bookkeeping 235

— Pan Wen'an

Recently, I saw in the newspaper an advertisement for the issuance of improved Chinese accounting books prepared by my friend Accountant Xu Yushu, and I was deeply gratified that this move would be sufficient to eliminate the bad habits of old-fashioned merchants and complete the work of accounting revolution. Currently, I am honored to have received a copy of "An Overview of Improving Chinese Bookkeeping" by Accountant Xu himself! After reading it, I felt that the key points of its reform were based on double-entry bookkeeping, while emphasizing the preservation of inherent conventions. This is a meticulous plan and a comprehensive design. It also has ingenious ingenuity.

In the past few years, I have followed the gentlemen in the national goods industry to promote the national goods business, supporting and assisting with all my strength. After several changes in winter and summer, I am ashamed that there is little success. Every year-end, I always review my past work, and I deeply feel that the results obtained are not proportional to our efforts. Although this kind of disappointment is said to be an inherent phenomenon in the vortex of the world's economic decline and domestic political instability, the incompatibility of China's economic and management system with the development of the social environment, and the failure of merchants' financial administration to enter the right track are also the main reasons: Please state as left;

(1) The malpractice of management system tending to westernization In recent years, people in the industrial and commercial circles have been aware of the prevalence of industrial rationalization in Europe, America and Japan, and have gradually realized the need to reform the management system. They have gradually imitated Europe and the United States in all facilities, and only followed the foreigners. However, the improvement of the system relies on self-sufficient equipment as an aid. In China, where the level of technology is still immature, all the equipment used under the new system is still far from the realm of self-sufficiency. In the end, the management equipment can only rely on foreign goods. My friend Jin Muyao said in his article "Management System and National Goods Movement"; "Before China opened to the sea, there was no relationship between the supply and demand of goods and the West. The items used by the people were self-produced and self-supplied, and there was no concept of using foreign goods. We only need to look at the equipment in the old-fashioned stores to understand this. The accounting books for receiving and paying from top to bottom, inkstones, pens, abacuses, book clips and other supplies are all local products; but since the reform, these old things have been abandoned with the change of the management system. The most capable expression of this phenomenon is a few brand-new banks. Bank bookkeeping is a new type of bookkeeping. Because it is written horizontally and uses international numbers, it has to use foreign paper, cloth-bound or leather-bound covers, as well as steel pens, pencils, inks and paper that are related to it, all of which must be foreign goods. Even the abacus, a special product of our country, is replaced by calculators from other countries. In this way, the management system is of course fully new, but the abandonment of national goods and the use of foreign goods has increased the import surplus in trade, which is a very serious problem. Even the newer the management system, the more westernized the items used. Therefore, in a certain sense, the abnormal innovation of the management system is a very uneconomical thing. In fact, the parties concerned did not intend to westernize, but felt that under the new management system, everything is more convenient in Western style." (Original text in Shenbao) can be said to be incisive. The way to promote national goods is to expand their sales, but under the current production environment in China, the improvement of the management system is enough to shrink the market for national goods. Such a serious contradiction is what people who are concerned about the national goods business are eager to solve.

(2) Insufficient accounting supervision It has been observed that the failure of factories and commercial firms is mostly due to the laxity of internal management and the malpractices of financial administration. To get to the root of the problem, it is nothing more than the failure of accounting supervision to be thorough. Because the old-fashioned accounting is chaotic in system, vague in items, and has no method of internal control. If precautions are neglected, malpractices will arise spontaneously. Moreover, the significance of accounting settlement is originally to guide the business policy of merchants and to express the financial situation: the organization of old-fashioned accounting books is not enough to talk about accounting principles, then its guidance to merchants' business is like a blind man riding a blind horse, and it is difficult for it not to collapse.

Accountant Xu advocates the improvement of Chinese bookkeeping, which will undoubtedly provide a lot of assistance in the reform of commercial management. The accounting books, pens and inks used are all domestic products, which is even more commendable. Utilizing the advantages of the new style and avoiding the first type of malpractice mentioned above is indeed a move that suits my heart. The recording, posting, settlement and table preparation procedures of the improved Chinese bookkeeping are all in line with the principles of double-entry bookkeeping, and the methods are simple and suitable for use by old-fashioned accounting personnel. In the future, if it is widely promoted, the financial malpractices of national goods manufacturers will be reduced as a result, and the second difficulty that we have been criticizing may also be solved easily. Our future work in promoting national goods may achieve twice the result with half the effort.

The contributions of improved Chinese bookkeeping to commercial management and accounting organization have been mentioned above. In addition to praying for good luck, I also believe that there are two points worth considering, and I would like to discuss them with Accountant Xu:

The Origin and Division of Eastern and Western Bookkeeping Methods 236

— Xu Yongzuo

Since there are human beings, there are written contracts, the system of recording numbers and the technique of arithmetic began. The preface of Xiahou Yang's Arithmetic Classic says: Arithmetic originated from Fuxi, and the Yellow Emperor set three numbers to ten levels, and Li Shou then wrote nine chapters. Ancient Italian history claims that the Mediterranean basin has a long history of recording numbers and events on metals or ceramics. It can be imagined that the relationship between the early number recording and arithmetic of the East and the West, and the calculation and bookkeeping techniques is close. However, in the beginning, human civilization was immature, and materials were not available; transactions and exchanges were rare; the tools for calculation and recording were also very heavy; therefore, the methods of arithmetic were still simple, and the tools for recording numbers were only for memorization! It is not possible to talk about bookkeeping methods.

As civilization progresses and the receipt and payment of wealth becomes more frequent, national and household economies become increasingly important. The art of calculation must be precise and consistent. The system of number recording must also be neat and easy to calculate. The art of bookkeeping gradually evolves. It can be seen from the emphasis on national accounting systems and arithmetic research in ancient civilizations in the East and the West. Those who have been good at accounting in our country since ancient times must be proficient in arithmetic, and the bookkeeping books left over from ancient Europe are often written by mathematicians. The evolution of bookkeeping methods with arithmetic is the same in the East and the West.

The influence of arithmetic on bookkeeping methods is like an equation. When discussing Eastern bookkeeping methods, the four-column clearing register method in our country is often used as its representative. When discussing Western bookkeeping methods, the double-entry recording method is often used as its representative. They are all regular and precise, and have a balanced calculation method. The four-column method and the double-entry method are both derived from the equation in arithmetic. The equation in the East developed very early. The eighth chapter of the Nine Chapters on the Mathematical Art is the equation chapter. This book was published before the Han Dynasty, so it can be imagined that the equation occurred early. Therefore, the four-column method was already popular in the Song Dynasty, no less than a thousand years ago. The equation in the West developed later. In 1494 of the Western calendar, Lucas Paciolo began to establish a special chapter in his book "Summa de Arithmetica, Geometria, Proportioni et Proportionalita" called "Particulalas de Computis et Lcripturis", applying this formula to bookkeeping, and producing the double-entry bookkeeping method, which is only four hundred and some years old. The changes in Eastern bookkeeping methods in modern times are all within the scope of the four-column clearing register method, and the changes in Western bookkeeping methods have not deviated from the rules of the double-entry bookkeeping method. The names of the two are different, but their origins from the equation are not different. It is intended that the method of recording numbers is mainly to facilitate arithmetic. Although there are various methods of arithmetic, the one that is convenient for the statistics and calculation of accounts is the equation. Therefore, no matter Eastern or Western, all the sages of bookkeeping can agree without prior consultation.

The Eastern four-column method divides the four columns for settlement, and the Western double-entry method corresponds to double-entry bookkeeping. Some people think that they are different. In fact, the four columns are old management, new receipt, removal, and actual. New receipt is total receipt, removal is total payment, and actual is closing receipt or closing payment. The actual in this period is the old management in the next period. In terms of Western-style various accounts, the total debit, the total credit, the debit difference or the credit difference; or the cash receipt and payment account, the previous balance, the current receipt, the current payment, and the current balance, what is the difference? The difference is that the old management of various accounts is also independent, so the comparison of the previous and subsequent, and the status of the process are more clear, unlike the Western style, which only establishes four columns in the cash account. This is in terms of the four-column method. Eastern and Western bookkeeping methods originally have common points. The original text of double-entry is Doubl eentry; Doppelbuchuug, meaning double-entry, whenever recording an account, it should be established simultaneously on the debit side and the credit side, in other words, each entry and exit must have two or more entries to make the debit and credit sides stand together. Whenever the account is closed and reported, each item should also be listed separately for debit and credit, so that it can be compared. The double-entry method created by Pacioli and the continental bookkeeping method that still exists today are all like this. However, as the organization of accounting books is gradually differentiated, each accounting book is based on a certain specific item, and only the corresponding item is recorded when recording an account. Therefore, in terms of each differentiated accounting book, the record is like a single entry. It is necessary to collect all accounting books for a summary observation to clearly show its double entry. The more differentiated the organization of accounting books, the more simple the records of each accounting book. The so-called double-entry or debit-credit comparison is almost only for the debit-credit comparison table. The method of double-entry has changed greatly. There are many examples in the current British and American double-entry bookkeeping methods. If these bookkeeping methods are all double-entry, then Eastern bookkeeping methods also have the same example. The various diaries are based on a certain special item, and the receipts and payments of the corresponding items are recorded. When the accounts of the cleaning book are entered into the balance sheet and the income statement, the receipts and payments are listed up and down for mutual comparison, and can be balanced and settled. This is the same as the spirit of Western double-entry. This is in terms of the double-entry method. Eastern and Western bookkeeping methods also have common phenomena.

The origin and laws of Eastern and Western bookkeeping methods have the common features mentioned above. However, those who are engaged in bookkeeping cannot fail to understand each other. What is the reason? In addition to the difference in text, there is also a major division. The recording of accounts in Eastern bookkeeping methods is divided into receipts and payments. The reason why receipts and payments are divided depends on whether the account is a receipt or payment for money. The recording of accounts in Western bookkeeping methods first distinguishes between debit and credit. The reason why debit and credit are distinguished depends on whether the other party of the account is a debtor or creditor for the operator. The former is subjective in dividing receipts and payments, and the latter is objective in distinguishing between debit and credit. Therefore, the receipts and payments in Eastern bookkeeping are the income or payment of money itself. For example, the income deposit is recorded in the income item; the debit and credit in Western bookkeeping are the debtor or creditor of the item itself. For example, the income deposit should be recorded on the credit side. In arithmetic, the arrangement of positive and negative numbers is exactly the opposite, the method of arithmetic is the same, and the balance of the equation obtained is also the same, but the starting point of number recording is different. The way to express the increase or decrease of property is also different. This is indeed a major division of Eastern and Western bookkeeping methods. Some people call Eastern bookkeeping method the receipt and payment bookkeeping method, and Western bookkeeping method the debit and credit bookkeeping method, precisely for this reason.

Although the nature of the Eastern receipt and payment bookkeeping method and the Western debit and credit bookkeeping method is different, they are consistent with the right track of number recording and arithmetic. Users have their own long history, so there is no need to force Liu Yi, and it is not appropriate to force uniformity. Therefore, those who study bookkeeping methods should first understand its origin, distinguish its divisions, and guide it in accordance with the situation. Since the end of the 19th century, Western bookkeeping methods have been introduced into the East. Those who are curious and show off do not know that the debit and credit bookkeeping method and the receipt and payment bookkeeping method come from the equation in arithmetic. The former's novelty is precious, and the latter's oldness is to be discarded. They often promote the former and suppress the latter, which is very confusing. Today's improved Chinese bookkeeping does not abandon the receipt and payment bookkeeping method because it is old-fashioned. They are diligently organizing and improving it with a scientific spirit. Those who understand the origin of number recording and arithmetic, and can distinguish the divisions of Eastern and Western cultures, should have the same feeling.

The Advantages of Improving Chinese Bookkeeping 237

— Wang Boyuan

All commercial receipts and payments, whether ancient or modern, Chinese or foreign, have book records to observe the increase or decrease of wealth and the profit or loss of business; although the types of businesses are different and the complexity of business is different, the accounting principles applied in bookkeeping are the same. The Chinese bookkeeping, which has been used in our country for generations, is often criticized by the world for its lack of organization and system. Today's scholars of accounting all despise Chinese bookkeeping, thinking that it is not worthy of learning, and all regard Western bookkeeping as the standard. However, the commercial practices of our country have been applied to each other for thousands of years, and they have not changed for a long time. To this day, except for a few new enterprises, the large and small businesses across the country still use them as before, so there must be something indelible in them. Bookkeeping is a practical and economical science. If it is practical and has economic effect, its effectiveness will be obvious. Although Western bookkeeping is more methodical and standard than Chinese bookkeeping, its theory is profound and its method is complicated. It is not easy to engage in it without considerable training. The cultivation of talents is costly, and paper and stationery are all foreign goods, which is costly and costly. On the contrary, the shortcomings of the Western style are the strengths of the Chinese style. If we can improve the shortcomings of the Chinese style, wouldn't it be more beautiful than the Western style? In short, there is no distinction between Chinese and foreign goods, and the system does not discuss the East and the West. Choosing the good and following it is the best. Mr. Xu Yongzuo is a pioneer in the accounting profession, proficient in his studies, and able to not agree with the public opinion, take the improvement of Chinese bookkeeping as his responsibility, and vigorously promote it, which is very insightful. The book "An Overview of Improving Chinese Bookkeeping" is easy to understand, the theory is thorough, and the equipment is comprehensive. The proposed samples of Chinese bookkeeping forms are clearly annotated, practical, and well-organized. They have the advantages of the Western style and the convenience of the Chinese style. As the author said, it is to seek universal progress for the Chinese accounting community, and I dare to believe that it is to seek universal benefits for the Chinese business community. The effect of this is great and beneficial, and it is also a great event in the academic world.

(1) The "Overview of Improving Chinese Bookkeeping" discusses the advantages and disadvantages of Chinese bookkeeping and the new procedures for registering accounts, setting the clauses for counterfeiting, listing the account forms, checking and issuing the gates, which are detailed and clear. Even those who have no knowledge of bookkeeping can manage it easily by following the rules and regulations. However, it may not be enough to talk about self-generation of changes and adapting to local conditions. Because each clause listed in the overview seems to be just a procedure on the surface, but behind it contains accounting theory. The advocates have a plan in mind, and they can change at any time and be successful in everything. However, the learners stick to the set pattern and do not know why, so we dare not believe that they can use it freely.

(2) Old-fashioned merchants inherit the traditional thinking and are immersed in the philosophy of "everyone sweeps the snow in front of their own door." It is really like asking the tiger for its skin to ask them to recognize the advantages and necessity of improving Chinese bookkeeping! In this merchant society that lacks automatic spirit, only the trade associations can persuade the counterparts to adopt it together from the standpoint of improving the management system and promoting business development; the government agencies can inform the merchants (at least those who are organized as companies) to strive for reform from the standpoint of promoting public integrity and protecting the interests of creditors.

The above two points are only for reference based on my personal feelings. I sincerely hope for it, so I can't help but think too much. 22, 12, 21, at the Four-Bank Savings Association

After Reading "An Introduction to Improved Chinese Bookkeeping" 238

— Xu Peikun

In the past decade or so, those in our country engaged in cashiering and accounting have largely been committed to adopting new-style bookkeeping. Government organizations, as well as companies and public groups in major cities, have gradually implemented and standardized their forms, books, and records. Indeed, the so-called scientification and rationalization of modern business operations have become almost universally adopted. Accounting manages the pivot of capital utilization, and bookkeeping is the factual record of account receipts and expenditures. Due to the limitations of the format, it has become a specialized discipline. It is true that our country cannot adhere rigidly to old methods and remain unchanged. The horizontal writing from left to right and the reliance on foreign goods for pens, ink, paper, and stationery are details that should not be overly scrutinized. However, I now have some doubts. What are these doubts? It is that the implementation of new-style bookkeeping may not be entirely suitable for China's national conditions. The purpose of learning is application, and modern scientists emphasize both theory and practice. In the past, I, being unworthy, held a position at the National Shanghai College of Commerce, and I always strived to cultivate practical talents. Therefore, whenever compiling curricula and selecting teaching materials, I repeatedly considered this objective. Bookkeeping and accounting are considered practical sciences. Practical sciences are diverse, but the key is to make promotion universal and their effect obvious as the sole principle. The accounting method of new-style bookkeeping must first involve debit and credit entries. Although settlement and reconciliation are based on academic principles, they can achieve the same result through different routes. However, the procedures are cumbersome, recording takes time, the underlying principles are difficult to understand, and it is easy to cause confusion. This is completely different from the old Chinese methods and is not easily understood by every household. Conversely, teachers and students studying bookkeeping today all say that banking bookkeeping is not difficult. They do not know that the old Chinese accounting method divides into four columns, with cash receipts and payments as the standard. The current banking accounting system's adoption of cash entry method does, in fact, subtly align with this, hence the saying that it is not difficult. Mr. Xu extracts the essence of the old method, eliminates the blockages of the new system, reconciling academic principles and returning to practicality, calling it "Improved Chinese Bookkeeping," which allows people to know at a glance that it is Chinese bookkeeping, pioneering the independence of our country's science. Its merit is immense. Moreover, its organization is clear, the procedures are concise, and its promotion is convenient. Scholars of the new learning, proficient in foreign sciences, obtain their secrets, but the lesser ones merely imitate the superficial aspects and despise everything Chinese, thinking it is all unworthy. This is the most extreme example of forgetting one's ancestors despite inheriting their legacy. What should Mr. Xu do? What should we do?

On Reading "An Introduction to Improved Chinese Bookkeeping" 239

— Yu Huan Cheng

I learned "Gu Bi" (old style bookkeeping) in my youth and am an amateur in accounting. My family had a shop, and I suffered from the lack of clarity and inconvenience of reviewing old-style bookkeeping records. I often changed it according to my own ideas, just to make it easier to review, without knowing the so-called academic principles. In the late Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, Teacher Tang Zhexian entrusted me with the responsibility of accounting for the Zhejiang Railway Company. At that time, the debate between new and old bookkeeping methods was quite intense. After more than half a year, it was impossible to complete the final accounts and report, which worried Teacher Zhe. The so-called new bookkeeping at that time was not double-entry accounting but only slightly modified the form, while those who advocated the old bookkeeping adamantly said it was not possible. In fact, neither side had any real understanding. After taking office, I groped my way forward, first defining the account subjects, then determining the types and organization of bookkeeping, and finally using the old method for the form, also referring to the Japanese railway bookkeeping format according to my own ideas. Fortunately, the final accounts were completed on time, and the report was correct. However, after working for half a year, I started before dawn and did not rest until midnight, working so hard that I almost became ill, and I asked for sick leave and left. What I was not satisfied with at that time was that I focused on the cost of road construction, so I strongly advocated that the purchase and receipt of materials must be entered into the accounting records through accounting, while the engineers and material supervisors believed that accounting was only in charge of cash and suspected that the consultant materials were exceeding their authority, arguing for several months without a solution. It was Zhu Jun Shoumen, the successor, who insisted on material price transfer, and the Ministry of Communications even awarded the Zhejiang Railway accounting as the best among the railways. At that time, the atmosphere was just opening up, and there were very few scholars who were familiar with bookkeeping, only engaging in large-scale projects for foreign merchants and borrowing money to build roads, learning the form but not knowing the principle, and unable to do anything when moved to another place, unable to implement double-entry bookkeeping. However, I firmly believe that the Chinese bookkeeping method can be used, but it depends on whether the general accountants will simplify it and do not know how to record and manage accounts, and also rely solely on books to enlighten them, resulting in fragmented and incomplete records, unable to fully perform the duties of verification and summary. This is my experience from twenty-eight years ago, which I often keep in mind. In recent years, I have helped a friend to reform the accounting of the China Merchants Group, and experts were hired to adopt double-entry bookkeeping, making the work easier (see the Accounting Regulations of the China Merchants Group, Mr. Xu Yushu, who is one of those in charge). Compared with the hard work and hardship of the Zhejiang Railway, the difference in work intensity is due to the times. Shanghai has been open to foreign trade for nearly a hundred years, but in terms of bookkeeping, even in large shops in commercial ports and among overseas Chinese merchants, the old style still accounts for nine out of ten, and the double-entry style accounts for less than one out of ten, not to mention the limitations of funding, talent, and customs in the interior. It is difficult to force it. Accountant Xu Yushu recently created "Improved Chinese Bookkeeping." I have been concerned with this issue for more than twenty years. Now someone has risen to answer it, and I cannot help but feel happy and amazed. I respectfully recount my memories and experiences to corroborate it. I dare to assert that the effectiveness of improved Chinese bookkeeping will far exceed the promotion of Western-style bookkeeping. As the Grand Historian Sima Qian said, "The best way is to follow the existing, the next best is to guide it." With the vast majority using old bookkeeping, and the improvements being thorough and easy to implement, its contribution to society, economy, law, and other aspects will be a great undertaking. Is Mr. Yushu practicing the way of "following the existing"? It is lofty and admirable. December 19, 1933.

Securities: Last Week's Bond Market Was Relatively Quiet 241

Most bonds fell by over one yuan over the week.

December futures have only two days left.

Last week, from December 18th to 23rd, the market activity at the Chinese Securities Exchange experienced fluctuations in the first half of the week and settled down in the second half. Although the December futures were very close to settlement, there was no major squeeze. Regarding the current situation, political maneuvering has given way to military means. Zhang Ji and his party will return to Beijing soon. The results of this trip are still unknown. Observing the central government's proactive approach to Fujian, on one hand, there is a general military mobilization, and on the other hand, an order to suppress is about to be issued, which may have obtained considerable understanding from the Southwest. The prospect of the war is unpredictable. Most market participants are taking a long position based on the assumption that the central government's military strength against one province should not be difficult. Others believe that the war will expand, and any setback will lead to a significant drop. Opinions are divided, and each has their own hopes. As a result, market prices have gradually become quieter. On Monday, due to the contact between Fujian and Zhejiang and the Japanese attempt to survey, major players sold off, causing prices to fall by a few "jiao" to over one yuan. On Tuesday, there were many rumors, including the reorganization of domestic and foreign debts, the re-emergence of the Third Government, and other unfounded rumors. Although it was known that they were inaccurate, many long positions were frightened out, causing market prices to plummet by one to two yuan. On Wednesday, the rumors subsided, and short positions made some adjustments, recovering about half a yuan in the morning. There was no market in the afternoon due to unforeseen circumstances. On Thursday, full-day trading of four sessions resumed, and the market became quieter. Although there was a large sale of the 75th issue, the market price fluctuated, indicating a balance. On Friday, short positions rolled over, and the 75th issue continued to be sold off, while the 16th and 21st issues saw considerable buying, causing the market price to rise by about one yuan. On Saturday, long and short positions rolled over, and the market price fluctuated, resulting in a slight gain of half a yuan. Over the week, most bonds fell by over one yuan. The total trading volume was 99,713,000 yuan. The December futures trading has only two days left. Essays

Empty Talk 244

— Shen Yan

In this age, speaking is indeed not easy. However, Heaven has endowed humans with the ability to speak, with good intentions, to give people another means of earning a living, in addition to fighting, running, jumping, and thinking. Looking at various countries in the East and West, whether in politics, business, or academia, those who occupy higher positions all have extraordinary eloquence. In other words, speaking is an innate ability given to humans, but there are great differences in skill, just like magic tricks. Those who can master these tricks will naturally have no problem making a living, and even getting promoted and becoming rich will not be difficult!

So, how should one begin to study the art of speaking? This is difficult! Because speaking is divided into dozens of categories, such as telling cold jokes, telling jokes, speaking dead words, boasting, speaking sarcastic remarks, complaining, lying, talking nonsense, and speaking lively words, each with its own unique skills, and it is impossible to learn them all at once! And among them, there is one most skillful and currently the most fashionable type of speaking: "empty talk," which is even more extraordinary!

However, phrases like "The weather is really nice today," "I think so too," "Whatever you think is fine," "I'll treat you to dinner in a few days," although they can be considered part of empty talk, are not subtle and straightforward, so people know you are just being perfunctory, which is not skillful at all. Truly clever people would never speak like this. Their empty talk is often the following two sentences.

The first sentence is "My power is insufficient." This sentence seems to be a firm refusal and not a perfunctory remark. They often express deep regret that they do not have the power to accept your request, appearing very sincere. However, how do you measure whether their power is truly "insufficient"? Even more admirable is that this sentence is soft on the surface but hard in reality. Even if you want to say a few more words, you can't, because they have already declared their inability to act. How can you force them?

The second sentence is "Nothing is impossible under heaven." This is such a philosophical statement! Although this sentence, if not spoken to someone who is asking you for something, can be categorized as "speaking dead words," it is actually the smartest and most skillful empty talk when someone is asking you for something. When people come to ask you for something, they often have a very serious expression on their face. After you say this, it's like pouring boiling water on clouds, and the situation will surely ease up. Even if you completely reject their request, they will not hate you. On the contrary, they will be very happy, thinking that you have given them the ultimate comfort in their hearts!

Leisure 245

— Zhou Limin

The two characters "leisure," in more common terms, means "free time."

We, the Chinese people, are all princes and grandsons after all, putting the serious national crisis, natural disasters, and man-made calamities behind us, indulging in pleasure, intoxicated in a world of gold and paper. Not to mention other things, just in social gatherings, when friends meet, they always ask, "What kind of entertainment have you been engaged in lately?" The other party will definitely answer, "Very leisurely, just doing some boring pastimes!" It can be seen that the leisure of your country's people truly lives up to the descendants of the Yellow Emperor!

Opium, cigarettes, Pai Gow, poker, yellow wine, brandy... these are our people's completely authentic leisure products; cafes, dance halls, movie theaters, massage parlors, teahouses, and taverns... those are our people's leisure places based on reason; the incapable A Dou who has nothing to do enjoys all the blessings in the world.

However, there are generally fools who are so bored with leisure that they worry about not being hungry after eating, causing trouble in the east and disaster in the west, making the world upside down and the people unable to live. What is the point?

In fact, there is no need to curse "leisure," and even less to eliminate "leisure." One should use many short leisure periods, leisure periods wasted by people, to pursue knowledge; such as the famous British statesman Gladstone, who always carried a small book with him, reading whenever he had free time. Therefore, over time, he accumulated vast knowledge. Another example is Faraday, the famous inventor in the field of electricity, who, while binding books for people, also conducted scientific experiments, writing to a friend, "What I need is time. I wish I could buy many empty hours or even empty days from 'leisurely people.'"

Find a way to eliminate leisure. Incapable A Dou who are idle, wake up!

The Apartment in the Old Capital 246

— Ping Fan

Leaving my beautiful hometown, Suzhou, I wandered to a corner of the north. With such shallow experience, I felt cold at heart when I arrived in an unfamiliar place. It wasn't an unhelpful act to have found a fellow villager who introduced me to a very quiet apartment!

Apartments are a unique type of lodging in the North. That apartment was in a remote area, making it the quietest of quiet places. There was a spacious field in front of the entrance, and the night view was even quieter. I love peace and quiet, so I felt very comfortable in my heart and wanted to write more.

"One, two, three...four." As soon as I started writing, a very disciplined sound came from outside. Children playing around wouldn't be so loud, but it didn't stop. All my thoughts of writing were driven away, and I couldn't put my pen down. I went outside to take a look. Four people in a row were wearing military uniforms. They were our revolutionary soldiers. Living in an apartment meant there would be military education and training. This was an unexpected harvest.

According to them, most of the residents of the apartment are students, and university students at that, so the calm sunlight passed over the window screens during the day. In the evening, pure plainsong, harmonicas, and foreign tunes that I couldn't name would begin to play. Although even in the middle of the night, there were still remnants of the melodies flowing.

I didn't find this kind of life annoying, because it was my first time testing it out.

These past few days have intensified. Not only is there military drill in the afternoon, but there's also a hasty bugle call before daybreak. The family next door played a talking machine all night long. I heard they invited friends over to play.

The North is not like Jiangnan. It just entered late autumn, and it started to snow. The ground was covered in white. The north wind howled. Each room had a coal stove installed. Rich people didn't care and used good coal chunks. Like several other people who didn't use coal chunks, I used coal briquettes. Burning coal briquettes can produce carbon monoxide poisoning. Someone was poisoned by the coal that day and drank a lot of sour cabbage soup. The next day, I also threw my coal stove in the corner of the yard.

The weather was very cold. I couldn't bear it without a stove, but I was afraid of being poisoned if I used one. I should go to bed earlier at night. The Huqin (Chinese violin) was playing "Si Lang Visits His Mother"... From "One, two, three... four" to "Charge! Kill!" I could only lie on the kang (heated brick bed) with my eyes open. Fine! I couldn't take it anymore. I said to the manager, "I might want to go to the south tomorrow. Or maybe move out!" I didn't actually mean it. But that evening, two people came to see the room. Business was really good! I don't know how there were so many customers.

The shop assistant said that a gentleman had been missing for a few days. Later, it was discovered that he had been taken away by the ×× team and locked up in the ×× Bureau, but no one knew what was going on.

"Poet's Lane" 247

— Chun Liu

Within the city limits of Nanjing, there are two lanes where the poetic atmosphere is richest: one is Longpan Lane in the west of the city, and the other is Cotton Shoe Camp in the east of the city.

Longpan Lane is a desolate lane sandwiched between Qingliang Mountain and Wulongtan, with one end closely connected to the mountains and fields. It is naturally rich in poetic flavor. Cotton Shoe Camp, however, is completely different from it.

This Cotton Shoe Camp, known as "Poet's Lane," is located in the middle of the bustling city. The north and south of it, such as Zhongzheng Street in the south and Changfu Street in the north, are both large roads in Nanjing. However, the street itself has a kind of quiet and solemn meaning, fully resembling a beautiful Song poem. The streets are neat, and the residents on both sides have water-milled brick walls. Almost every house has many ancient trees extending from within the walls. These trees are either elm trees, paulownia trees, or桫 trees. When deep autumn arrives, the streets are full of late yellow fallen leaves. In particular, the row of houses on the east side of the street, because behind them is one of the most beautiful curves of the "Nine Curves of Qingxi," each house has a water pavilion built. When we sail on the Qinhuai River, we can identify that is the Lan Garden, that is the Jian Garden, and the Spring Garden.

The owners of these houses are almost all "poets." For example, Jian Garden belongs to Wu Jianquan, and Spring Garden was originally named Hao Hall and belongs to Zheng Xiaoxu (of course, there is no need to talk about him now). Mr. Chen Sanli's former Sanli Villa is not far from here.

The last time I walked through this "Poet's Lane," I accidentally broke into a few gardens to take a look, and they all revealed a sense of decline. I heard that the owner of a certain house is in the most dire straits, owing more than a dozen months of housing donations to the Municipal Bureau. I couldn't help but think of a poem by a Song Dynasty poet: "The thatched eaves have a tax for the moon, and there is no rent for a single grain of rice. Life is bleak, and people ask me about the water banana and the calamus."

The Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 248

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: Divination Promises Good Fortune, the Old Man Laughs Away His Worries Day After Day; Old Friends Reside Across the Street

He thought about the two things together, and inevitably thought of them as one thing. So, a flush rose on his face, and even the roots of his ears began to feel hot. Because his face was also hot, he didn't dare to look at his mother, turned over to the inside, and half-closed his eyes to sleep. He heard Jiang Shi say, "What time is it? Still sleeping? Get up." Guizhi didn't say anything and continued to sleep on her side. Jiang Shi said, "Is your body not well again? Get up and sit for a while, don't really sleep yourself sick." Guizhi was about to speak, but her mother's hand had already touched her forehead. She said, "Oh! Your forehead isn't very hot. Why is your face a little flushed?" At this time, it was impossible for Guizhi not to pretend to be sick, so she dragged out a soft voice and said, "Maybe I caught a gust of wind when I went out yesterday, and the illness flared up again. "That's nothing to worry about. I'll sleep until ten o'clock, restore my energy, and the illness will be fine." Jiang Shi laughed and said, "Where is there still ten o'clock? Wait until tonight. It's almost time for lunch." Guizhi stretched out her hands from the cotton quilt, stretched lazily, and smiled, "I really didn't expect that I would sleep until this time in a daze. This is terrible." As she spoke, she grabbed her clothes from the edge of the kang, draped them over herself, and walked down from the kang. She walked to the window, stretched her head out to look outside, to see what time it was. The sky was not clearly visible, but a mirror leaning against the table reflected her face, which was yellowish, and her eye sockets seemed to have sunken quite a bit. After seeing this, she couldn't help but be startled in her heart. How could a day of illness make her so sick? No wonder people say that lovesickness can kill people. Only I know about this kind of thing. If my mother knew, she would say that I, this girl, am not behaving properly. Besides, Zhao Ziqiang is very loyal to me. If I don't marry him, I won't marry him. He can't blame me. Now that I am marrying him, why am I being fickle? That's it! From now on, I will definitely not care about any Second Master Gan or Third Master Gan. When she thought of definitely not caring, she made up her mind one hundred and twenty percent. At that moment, she stomped her foot on the ground. Jiang Shi, seeing her from behind, said in unison, "What's wrong? You're getting anxious again. What is it?" (276)

World Oddities

— Bing Yu

Eccentric Encoffined Living 249

A man in Chicago named York Robin, recently had an outlandish idea, he prepared two months of dry food and water, climbed into a coffin buried underground and hid. Before carrying it out, he earnestly told people, but refused to reveal the location, fearing that his family would come looking. Later, he did indeed safely spend two months living in the coffin. One day, a car stopped by the tomb, and he emerged from the coffin, got into the car, and returned home, while guiding relatives and friends to inspect the underground coffin. This story has now spread throughout the city of Chicago.

Hen With the Most Eggs 250

The American Minister of Agriculture, organized an all-England hen egg-laying championship. A few days ago, he announced the hen that laid the most eggs, a large Irish hen from Lancashire. This hen continued to lay eggs for forty-eight weeks, that is, within three hundred and thirty-six days, it laid two hundred and ninety-nine eggs, winning the first prize. There were two others that could lay two hundred and fifty eggs per year, and countless that laid less than two hundred eggs.

Praying for Overly Long Life 251

Generally, no matter who it is, except in special circumstances, everyone hopes for a long life. There is no one who does not want to live longer. In the United States, in Kings County, there is an old man named Samuel Clay, who is now a hundred years old. Every day, before going to bed at five o'clock in the afternoon, he holds the statue in his chest and prays, saying, "For people in the world, living to eighty years old is most appropriate. I am already a hundred years old this year, and I think I am extremely unwilling. Please God help me to die early." He believes that living twenty years longer means consuming twenty years more of living resources, and he often remembers the ancient saying that to be old and not die is to be a thief.

Strange Heart 252

In Romania, there was a young farmer named Olatay, who committed suicide with a pistol as a result of unrequited love. Two bullets penetrated from the left chest. When the family heard the gunshot, they immediately ran in to rescue him, all thinking that he could not be saved. Later, he was sent to the hospital, and after an X-ray, his heart was on the right side and was not fatally injured. After the operation, he fully recovered.

Million Dollar Painting 253

In the early fifteenth century, a famous painting by a master of the Venetian school, Chiara Xia Shi, titled "The Great Storm," was recently purchased by the Italian Fascist government for five million lire (equivalent to one million of our country's currency). It is said that the true value is more than twice that amount.

World of Bathrobes 254

This summer, the heat in Hungary is unprecedented in centuries. Therefore, not only in resorts do people wear bathrobes, but throughout the country, regardless of men, women, old, or young, people only wear extremely thin bathrobes when going out. However, the government believes that wearing only bathrobes hinders customs, so women on the streets are interfered with by the police every day and subjected to violation of police laws, resulting in an overwhelming situation that cannot be dealt with.

Our Encounters 255

— Cao Juren

Mr. Chen Hengzhe returned from a trip to the United States and gave a lecture at Yenching University on some of his impressions of revisiting North America. Among them, he spoke of the gloomy fog of unemployment panic that the American intellectual class was suffering from. He encountered six classmates in the United States, all of whom were university graduates with knowledge and talent above the average, and some even had unique skills. "But none of them did not feel the panic of unemployment. Those with positions felt the instability of their positions, and those without positions felt the difficulty of finding jobs." One of them even said to Mr. Chen: "If you don't help me go to China, I'll just have to jump into the Hudson River!" "Everywhere is desolate, and the world is in darkness." The plight of American intellectuals is so pitiful; compared to our Chinese intellectuals, it's "a close call"! American university graduates have to jump into the Hudson River, and our poet did indeed jump into the Yangtze River.

Some people say that jumping into the river to commit suicide is "weak-willed"; weakness of will may be a factor; but what if the will is strong? Ferri (an Italian criminologist) said: "There is nothing more harmful to the human mind and body than hunger. Hunger is the root of all inhuman and antisocial emotions; on the hunger line, there is no love, no human affection possible." On the hunger line, a strong will manifests as breaking the law and violating prohibitions. The so-called intellectuals do not have the courage to break the law and violate prohibitions; they are wearing long gowns and are embarrassed to step out of the circle of propriety; therefore, there are only two paths to take: one is to sell oneself, and the other is to commit suicide. Those who are unwilling to sully their personality have no choice but to "commit suicide." Qu Yuan wandered along the riverbank, haggard and emaciated; the fisherman told him: "The sage does not cling to things, but is able to move with the world. The world is all muddy, why not stir up its waves? Everyone is drunk, why not feed on its dregs and sip its lees?" Qu Yuan said: "I have heard that those who have just washed their hair will surely flick their hats, and those who have just taken a bath will surely shake their clothes. How can I use my clean body to accept the dirt of things? I would rather go to the Xiang River and be buried in the belly of the river fish, than to cover my bright whiteness with the dust of the world." In the moment of great liberation, Mr. Zhu Xiang must have felt proud enough to say, "Return my clean body!"

When Wang Yangming buried his belongings in Longchang, he tearfully told his servant, "You and I are like them!" Mr. Zhu Xiang's encounter is our encounter. During this year, one of my friends sacrificed himself for others because of hunger, leaving behind an old mother and an orphaned daughter. Another friend had a severe attack of appendicitis and, at the time of his death, was still calculating where he could pre-draw his monthly salary and when the employment contract would be sent, but in the end, there was not enough for a coffin. Are these tragic endings not as heartbreaking as Mr. Zhu Xiang's suicide by jumping into the river? Is it only the vast waves that are our final resting place?

I Also Talk About Nalan Chengde 256

— Chen Zizhan

Thank you, Mr. Chen Liang, for introducing Nalan Chengde's poetry theory, because the Lushuiting Miscellany is not easy to find. In this poetry theory, it is precisely proved that Nalan Chengde's ci poetry is nothing special, and his slap just hit his own face.

When classical poetry declined, ci poetry arose; when ci poetry declined, the opera lyrics arose; when the opera lyrics declined, Nalan Chengde knew this. At that time, Kunqu Opera still had some remaining strength. Why didn't he write opera lyrics but wrote ci poetry? He said, "Writing poetry is to express feelings. According to the current world, modern-style poetry is enough to express feelings." I also think this is very true. Why doesn't he write modern-style poetry when he picks up his pen to express feelings, but writes ci poetry, which has been abandoned for a long time? He said, "Those who love the past have no real feelings and forcibly imitate their forms to write ancient yuefu, which is particularly meaningless." Is it that those who love the past have no real feelings and forcibly imitate their forms to write ci poetry, which is considered to be particularly meaningful? He said, "In the Song Dynasty, songs and lyrics, and the methods of Tang Dynasty singing poetry were abandoned; when Yuan Dynasty opera lyrics arose, ci poetry was abandoned; when Southern opera lyrics arose, Northern opera lyrics were abandoned. In today's world, singing 'Deer Cry' is like serving dusty rice and smearing mud." In those days, singing the elegant music "Deer Cry" was indeed like serving dusty rice and smearing mud. Ci poetry is no longer singable, and no one sings it. It is not even as good as dusty rice and smeared mud. Why does he insist on eating ci poetry as food? His poetry theory is "anti-imitationism," which I also admit, but he himself is a complete imitationist poet. Although, he also has so-called self-composed tunes, but they are probably not singable, so they cannot be considered creations.

In the history of ci poetry, the first idol was Li Houzhu, and the last idol was Nalan Chengde. Some people even say that Nalan Chengde is the incarnation of Li Houzhu. This is truly nonsense. Wang Guowei proclaimed himself the number one person after Nalan Chengde, so he most complimented Li Houzhu and also greatly complimented Nalan Chengde. Among the ci poets of the Qing Dynasty, Wang Guowei only saw Nalan Chengde, and all the other families were not in his eyes. What is so special about Nalan Chengde?

He was the son of Grand Scholar Mingzhu, a bodyguard of Emperor Kangxi, with a comfortable life, superior education, and a beautiful environment. If he was not born an idiot and was willing to use his considerable talent in filling in ci poetry, getting considerable achievements would not be considered anything. Moreover, the main characters depicted in ci poetry during its heyday were no more than the sons and beautiful women who were the embodiment of the special class, and the actual life depicted was nothing more than the special class enjoying fine wine, women, and singing. For a rich and romantic playboy like Nalan Chengde to imitate such ci poetry, it was naturally possible to succeed. Coincidentally, his beloved wife died, and his mourning for the dead and sighing for the past unconsciously flowed between the lines, covering it with a very strong sentimental atmosphere. Coincidentally, he served as a bodyguard and often accompanied the emperor on tours, horseback riding, shooting, and suburban hunting, which aroused his feelings of frontier melancholy. At the same time, he was a successful candidate in the imperial examination and proclaimed himself elegant, and was able to associate with great celebrities such as Yan Shengsun, Gu Zhenguan, Jiang Chengying, and Chen Weisong. Therefore, he rescued Wu Zhaoqian, a friend exiled to Ningguta, for Gu Zhenguan. This kind of passion and chivalry also became part of his ci poetry, and it was the part most praised by literati. The biographies in the History of the Qing Dynasty said that his ci poetry was widely copied and spread throughout villages, schools, and post walls, which may not be entirely exaggerated. If we want to say what is so special about Nalan Chengde's ci poetry, I think it is here.

"Opening one's mouth to write, even four horses cannot catch up, is not an easy task." That rich and romantic playboy who proclaimed himself talented, if the Lushuiting Miscellany had not discussed poetry and ci poetry and "rashly cursed," he would have given people less material to scold.

Rice Harvesters 257

— Sheng Huanming

When the rice ears are heavy enough to droop, one can see "rice harvesters" continuously on the official road, almost at any time. They carry a straw mat package and some scattered items and a few changes of clothes on the other end of the bamboo pole. Panting, they walk past with an accent from a place one or two hundred miles away.

At this time, families with more fields have to plan how many rice harvesters to hire this year. Rice harvesters are mostly hardworking and rarely unreliable. They are mostly people from the eastern part of the country, because the harvest season there is later than ours, so they take this opportunity to leave home and travel to other places to earn some money, or bring something back.

The harvest season in my hometown is indeed particularly early. The weather is still so hot and sultry, but the rice can be harvested. Precisely because of this, the rice harvesters can rest on the thirteen-hole large stone bridge that connects the countryside and the town before being hired. Their temporary home is this open-air bridge, and life is certainly difficult. When children see rice harvesters passing by, they will hum a song mocking them: It is said that rice harvesters have to pick up watermelon rinds on the bridge to chew to quench their thirst. This situation may be true, because quite a few people are penniless before being hired.

After the harvest season is determined, families needing short-term help go to the area around the large stone bridge to find rice harvesters. Because there are many rice harvesters, the selection is particularly harsh. If they are hired particularly early, then those penniless rice harvesters who are eager to be hired must also have their wages discounted using the principle of "supply and demand." Or, if they are hired particularly late, the rice harvesters will inevitably be devalued even more.

As for my family's rice harvesters, there is a fixed rule: when the time is almost right, the four old rice harvesters always come themselves. They are a family, and they also bring some local specialties when they come. They are like distant relatives to each other. Grandfather waves a wheat stalk fan and talks to them intimately about the crops of the year. They have been used by grandfather since he was a young man! For twenty years, these four rice harvesters, except for Gui Tu, have all been replaced by their descendants, but this does not damage the trust between them.

"Gui Tu and the others should have come, why..." Because the time is urgent, Grandfather becomes anxious.

"Let's hire a few from the big bridge first!" says "Chang Nian".

Grandfather is unwilling to accept this. Twenty years of feelings and trust cannot make him do that. He looks at the golden field in front of him, sighs, and slowly walks towards the field.

Gradually, the village is filled with a strong fragrance of rice straw. Grandfather finally paces anxiously towards the distant official road and sighs, "Alas! I really didn't expect! Didn't expect!"

In the evening, an old guest appeared outside the gate, not much different in age from Grandfather. He wiped the sweat from his forehead with his sleeve and coughed. It was Old Guest Gen Tu from eight years ago, the rice harvester Grandfather praised the most twenty years ago.

Grandfather is obviously stunned, but then he is so moved that his voice becomes hoarse: "Old man, we are all useless!"

The guest looks at Grandfather with a sallow gaze and sighs, "Alas, Uncle Rong, hasn't your rice started harvesting yet? I'm sorry to you this year! They can't come!"

"Why?" Grandfather is stunned, and the dry tobacco pipe slides down from the corner of his mouth.

"Yes, Uncle Rong, they can't come this year. My brother... Gui Tu, passed away in the spring!"

"Ah..." Grandfather's sallow eyes shine brightly.

"Those two children are useless and have both become soldiers, Uncle Rong, that is my fault. Our few mu of rented land have all been returned. What can three mu of 'already tilled land' provide for a family of four? 'Forced to Liangshan'... I'm really sorry to you this year, Uncle Rong, I specially came to send a message because I felt bad, have you not hired any helpers yet?"

"Haven't hired... Haven't hired..." Grandfather replies absentmindedly. "I was waiting for you to come, Gen Tu, why did you have to let your children go 'become soldiers and eat grain'? Good men don't become soldiers, and good iron doesn't become nails, you you, does Gui Tu have any sons or daughters left?"

"No, he never married, he lived this life alone, I really feel sorry for my parents."

"You should recruit one back, descendants are important," Grandfather says, coughing, "Descendants... you have to send a message to recruit one back..."

× × × × ×

After that, whenever the rice ears are heavy enough to droop, Grandfather always stares with his old eyes at the golden field when he sees rice harvesters on the official road; he murmurs to his children and grandchildren about Gen Tu and his descendants.

Two Brothers (6) (9) 258

— Translated by Maupassant, Li Weike

She looked like she was going mad. He was terribly frightened, and suddenly knelt in front of the bed and said softly:

"Don't say it, Mom, don't say it."

She stood up with astonishing determination and willpower.

"But I have nothing else to say to you, my child, farewell."

She walked towards the door.

He stretched out his arms and hugged her, shouting:

"What are you doing, Mom, where are you going?"

"I don't know... How would I know... I have nothing else to do... Because I'm all alone now."

She struggled to escape. He grabbed her, he could only repeatedly shout:

"Mom... Mom... Mom..."

She struggled to break free from his arms, saying:

"Don't hold me, don't hold me, I'm not your mother anymore, I have no relationship with you or anyone else anymore, no relationship at all! You have neither a father nor a mother, my poor child... Farewell."

He suddenly realized that if he let her go, he would never see her again, so he picked her up, placed her in an armchair, and forced her to sit down. Then he knelt in front of her and blocked her with his arms:

"You must not leave this place, Mom; I love you, I want to keep you. I want to keep you forever, you belong to me."

She said softly in a subdued voice:

"No, my poor child, this is impossible. Tonight you cry, and tomorrow you will throw me out the door. You"

You won't forgive me either."

He replied with such fervent and genuine love: "Ah! Me? Me? How little you understand me!" Hearing this, she was so moved that she let out a cry, grabbed his head with both hands, pulled him violently towards herself, and passionately kissed him.

Then she stood motionless, pressing her face tightly against her son's face, feeling the heat of his flesh through the stubble; she leaned close to his ear and whispered:

"No, my little Zhe'an. You won't forgive me tomorrow. You think you will forgive me, but that's unreliable. You forgave me tonight and saved my life because of it; but I have to let you not see me again."

He hugged her tightly, repeating:

"Mom, don't say that!"

"Really, my good baby, I have to go. I don't know where to go, I don't know what to do, I don't know what to say, but I have to go. If I don't go, I won't dare to look at you, I won't dare to kiss you, do you understand?"

So this time he also leaned close to her ear and said softly:

"Dear Mom, you will stay here, because I want it that way, because I need you. You have to swear to listen to me right now."

"No, my child."

"Ah! Mom, it has to be this way, do you hear? It has to be this way."
