Eugenics Law 259

— Non-human

A Reuters dispatch from Havana on the 20th reports that the German government's law on eliminating reproductive function is scheduled to take effect on January 1st of next year. It is estimated that approximately 400,000 people suffering from hereditary diseases will be subject to this law.

After reading this telegram, a thought suddenly occurred to me. Our esteemed nation, notoriously known as the "sick man of Asia," is renowned throughout the world. If this law were implemented in our country, I fear that the number of people subject to it would not be limited to 400,000, but rather 4 million, or even 40 million, would still not be enough. However, if this law could truly come to our esteemed nation, it would not only promote eugenics but also be a splendid plan for national salvation, as our nation's problems are often rooted in the mischief of reproductive function.

From the perspective of our esteemed nation, the most significant and common harm caused by reproductive function is the corruption of morals and customs. This is because our nation's maxim, "A wife is not as good as a concubine, a concubine is not as good as a prostitute, a prostitute is not as good as a maidservant, and a maidservant is not as good as a stolen affair," is deeply understood by our people. As a result, in court cases related to public morals, nine out of ten cases are about this. If Germany's law were implemented in our country, not only would the court presidents and judges save much trouble, but would our ethical teachings not be better maintained and preserved? This point, of course, is a very small benefit.

If we extend this further, with reproductive organs, the first thing needed is a family. With a family, there are children, then grandchildren, then great-grandchildren, and then great-great-grandchildren and countless descendants. If there is a family, then there is a need to maintain the family's economy, and therefore there is a need to accumulate wealth to maintain the economy for generations to come. If this cannot be maintained, then people resort to deception, plunder, theft, robbery, and extortion. All kinds of wrongdoing and crimes arise from the reproductive organs.

Especially in our esteemed nation, which is currently plagued by overpopulation, widespread unemployment, natural and man-made disasters, and widespread poverty, if Germany's "law on eliminating reproductive function" were applied to all 400 million people in our country, it would be a comprehensive solution. If the population were not excessive, there would be no widespread unemployment panic. Without unemployment panic, there would be less competition, theft, and crime. However, this law must be renamed; it should not be called the Eugenics Law, but rather the "Euthanasia Law."

The people of our esteemed nation have not studied other fields, but everyone has researched eugenics. Not only have they researched it, but they are also experts in it. If you don't believe me, I will give two examples as proof. Not only are Little Si Zi and Little San Zi in Hebei highly knowledgeable, but look at the women begging in Jiangbei. Not only do they hold one child in their arms, but they also carry one and follow with another. Perhaps in the thatched shed, there are several older children carrying baskets, selling roasted chestnuts or peanuts. As for the residents of Shanghai, in one lane, there are only ten or twenty house numbers, but the number of children gathered there often reaches forty or fifty. The output of this kind of manufacturing is certainly extremely abundant.

Currently, there are several compassionate and wise people who often lament natural and man-made disasters, often lament the ceaseless wars, and the killing of people like flies. I think if every year were blessed with favorable weather and the world were at peace, according to biological principles, there would be more than 400 million people, perhaps even more than 1 billion people, and the population would still be excessive, and unemployment would still be a panic. From this point of view, the demon kings who kill people are actually the true saviors of the world, so Jesus has his own reasons. Amen.

Christmas Gifts 260

— Li

It was the evening of the day before Christmas. Dark clouds filled the sky. From the seemingly low horizon, a kind of gloomy and desolate color was emerging. The excessive accumulation of moisture in the air was mixed with the towering annual red lights of Wing On Department Store and Sincere Company on Tibet Road, forming a pinkish haze that enveloped the entire downtown area. The cold wind blowing from the northwest at this time fully displayed its power, giving pedestrians on the road a bone-chilling sting; hitting the walls of tall buildings, it twisted and turned, emitting a miserable and sharp cry. This kind of cold and gloomy weather prompted the thought of pressing hard for repayment of debts.

At this time, the red and blue lights of the racecourse's red-lettered announcements had begun to flash on and off in a rhythmic pattern, and the long and short hands of the clock below were paired up and down, forming a vertical line. The streets were particularly crowded tonight. Every public bus and tram was packed like a lottery drum, filled with bipedal animals, and at each stop, it struggled to swallow and spit out piles of people. The cars, head to tail, each opened their dazzling eyes, and under the direction of the traffic lights, dozens of them lined up in a straight line, advancing slowly with their engines running. Cries of "Great Evening News!" "Great American Evening News, five copper coins!" quickly filled the major streets and alleys.

At the corner of the New Hotel on Great New Street, a very weak plea suddenly arose along the road: "Boss! Do a good deed! Cultivate blessings and longevity, many sons and grandsons, have pity on the poor... Give a copper coin to buy a bowl of congee... Boss! Sir!" This was exactly the set of "verses" that the beggar "Lame Ah Yi" could recite backwards, and he was chasing after a passing "gentleman" at this time.

As a result of the relentless pursuit and the increasingly rapid recitation of the verses, "where there's a will, there's a way," he brazenly received from the eyes of the passing "gentleman" a look that combined "sniffing," "annoyance," "disgust," "impatience," and "get lost," followed by a toss! Although it was only a copper coin, because it was thrown with force, it landed in Ah Yi's dry and chapped hand, but it seemed very heavy! This copper coin was labeled "No. 10" in Ah Yi's pocket, such an "unlucky" number!

Generally speaking, every down-and-out person nearing the age of "knowing destiny" has had a golden age in their past life, a time when they were "quite something..." Lame Ah Yi was naturally no exception.

When he was twenty years old, when he was said to be "a real hero," he had already climbed from "brother" to "logistics officer" under Marshal Wang, becoming at least a "lieutenant" officer, a platoon leader. He had fought more than once, but: why fight? Who to fight? These were too profound questions for him to understand. At that time, Feng Guozhang was still the President, and of course there were no such things as "punishing counter-revolutionaries" or "suppressing the communists." Once, during a troop mobilization, the marshal had given a "lecture" to officers of all levels. Unfortunately, this platoon leader was sitting too far away, and only saw the marshal foaming at the mouth and shouting, "Brothers! Fight hard! Beat that bastard Zhao ××'s bastard son!" A wave of "oaths" followed.

Unfortunately, as a result of fighting the "bastard son" that time, Ah Yi got injured, which was the end of his "logistics officer" life, and the origin of his becoming "Lame Ah Yi." Afterwards, Ah Yi went from being a lane administrator to becoming the "street inspection commissioner" begging along the street.

Today, it happened to be the night before the "carnival night" of the upper class, and the ladies and gentlemen on the road were busy buying things; who still cared about the "lowly wretches" like "Lame Ah Yi"! Ah Yi started working at three o'clock, begging the bosses and madams, and now, besides the "thirteen taels" of copper coins in his pocket, he also had half a dozen cigarette butts picked up from under the feet of people at various tram stops.

He circled several streets, and finally turned from the New World to the Great World, dragging his heavy and weak legs, moving towards the Bund. The method of reciting "verses" to passersby was extraordinarily ineffective today, only succeeding once in ten attempts. Later, under the excessive gaze of passersby, he simply stopped begging and concentrated on looking at the displays in the brightly lit stores. Inside the glass windows, in addition to the usual Christmas scenes, with one or two white-haired, rosy-cheeked, smiling Santa Clauses and red and green Christmas trees, there were also various colored chocolates, pastries, piles of canned goods, and large and small bottles of foreign wine. The aroma of hot dishes being fried and braised constantly wafted from the various restaurants and snack shops, directly assaulting Ah Yi's nostrils. He felt that his long-panicked internal organs were not only "shouting slogans" at this time, but also beginning to "stir"!

The short hand of the Hendali clock on the bowling alley had already pointed to the number "two." His two legs, so tired that they were almost broken, dragged Ah Yi across from the Cathay Hotel to the entrance of the Palace Hotel. Inside the glass, foreign gentlemen, high-class Chinese, ladies, and socialites were embracing and dancing with each other in an atmosphere of bright lights, fine wine, and melodious music. Ah Yi couldn't help but stare in a daze, while also thinking about the "flower girls" he had played with when he was a "logistics officer." He unconsciously stepped onto the stone steps, stretching his neck like a heron, looking inside and forgetting himself more and more. Suddenly, an "Ah San" (Indian doorman) with a "mourning stick" rushed out from inside, "as usual" kicking him in the butt, while muttering in Pidgin English: "Damn you! Get out!"

Lame Ah San woke up from his daze. He also received a kind of "Christmas gift" - a foreign "ham"!

Ominous News on a Rainy Night 261

— Ding Ding

The early winter season has finally arrived, following the late autumn. Everything presents the phenomenon of winter. It is raining again, and the rain is not light. The sound of raindrops hitting the roof tiles is very audible. The world is so quiet, only the ticking of the clock and the gurgling of the water flowing from the eaves. Ah! It must be about eleven o'clock! Last night at this time was the last second after Ms. Wen's death. Ah? She has been dead for a whole day. Only her mother was at the burial. She is probably only twenty-two years old this year. Ah! I remember, my reunion with her after our first separation was on the evening of Fourth Road's ×× Restaurant. That night, because my uncle had just returned to the countryside, my mother and brother invited him to have dinner at ×× Restaurant. My uncle said that he heard in the countryside that there were snow-white young girls in Shanghai's brothels, specializing in lewd business... So my mother ordered my brother to write three invitations and send them to the tea room, inviting them so that my uncle could see what Shanghai's so-called prostitutes were. After the invitations were sent, we still talked about our own serious business, but only heard the sound of "woo woo ya ya" fiddles and clear singing from the small rooms on both sides.

A prostitute walked in, followed by a "young gentleman" and a "blind teacher" waiting outside. "Who is it for?" she asked as she sat down next to my brother. "No, I asked you to come and show this old man, go and sit next to this old man and talk to him." This was my brother's brief reply, pointing to my uncle. "Did your blind teacher come? Sing a song for us!" This was my mother's words, and so our small room began to sing.

The second "courtesan" also came in. "Alas! Why do you good women have to do this shameful thing? Is there nothing else you can do? You unfortunate girls are simply entering a living hell!... Is it one dollar for a call? Okay, take it and go." My uncle raised his old eyes and looked at the prostitutes, giving them each one dollar and telling them to leave. "Ah! These women are truly the scum of women, they are willing to engage in this kind of career, men's playthings, human parasites..." I looked at their retreating figures and scolded them sharply.

The third prostitute who was invited finally came. Ah! I couldn't believe my eyes: wasn't she Wen? I cried out. She saw me, her face full of shame and shrinking back secretly. Although it was only for a moment, I could be sure that it was Wen, my classmate in junior high school. So I remembered what a friend had told me about her. It was probably because her family was under economic pressure, her parents sacrificed her lifelong happiness, this daughter who was a beautiful female student, like a commodity. Because she wanted to save her innate freedom, she struggled and declared her separation from her family. At that time, she had an ambition: she wanted to use her limited junior high school knowledge to make a living independently! But alas: life is too harsh for young people, she was blocked everywhere and cruelly鞭策! So she entered the brothel and took on the career of her flesh.

It must be eleven o'clock, Ms. Wen has been dead for a whole day. The weather continues to get colder and faster, and the rain has not stopped, falling, falling, where is the phenomenon of winter!

Homesickness 262

— Wanting to Return

City Correspondence Two

Villagers;

Coming out of the newspaper office, it was already dusk. I buried my head in the high collar of my coat and stepped onto the sidewalk of Nanjing Road. This is a crazy world. Cars chase after trams crazily. The swift feet of rickshaw pullers are also exceptionally strong. The light of the neon lights makes people not believe that Shanghai has day and night. Even the blind female beggar who begs for a copper coin with a bitter face is unusually lovely. I want to go back to my resting place as soon as possible. I have no attachment to this world—this crazy world. I quicken my pace and walk forward, but am stopped by the waist of a woman swimming like an eel. She is so light. The lower part of her silk cheongsam is blown by the crazy wind. The waltz steps are so charming. I seem to have fallen into the embrace of spring; but the eel woman's neck is clearly wearing a black fur collar, so I try to raise my head and take a perspective review of this crazy world. In front of the fruit shop opposite, a female chimney made of lead pipes rises up, like Mei Lanfang's stage performance, surrounded by countless bright electric lights, a sign of Liangxiang chestnuts is powerfully imprinted into my brain nerves. I don't believe in the seasons of Shanghai. Is there such a big difference on both sides of a road? I was thinking about how I ran into this crazy world, and followed the beautiful lines forward. By the time I remembered that I came out of the gloomy newspaper office editorial room, the eel-like body had entered a silk shop. I raised my head and saw that their banner also clearly read "Winter" sale, at this time I affirmed that "Winter" has come, but in this crazy world, even the blind female beggar who begs for a copper coin with a bitter face is unusually lovely!

I quickly ran home. Villagers, my home is a small pavilion room of less than ten square feet. The landlord will not turn on the lights until six o'clock. It is already dark. I pulled out a cigarette and lay on the army bed I bought for three dollars. Then fantasy reflected from my brain. Fortunately, we poor people still have this right. For example, it is clear that it is a waste of one dollar, but the hope of 50,000 yuan can always make you dream of being a rich man for a few days.

It's winter. I wonder if the holly tree in my backyard has been trimmed so neatly? Ah Huo is a lazy child. When I am at home, he always has a share in all the naughty tricks. If I want him to do something, unless I lie to him that he will not be allowed to eat dinner tonight, he will not do anything. Counting carefully, I have not returned home for five years. Five years of time have turned myself into a fifty-year-old man. Ah Huo will not be the same as when he was thirteen years old. He must have already trimmed the holly tree neatly, and all the withered weeds have been removed, or he can already help the farmhand with the rice harvest. Ah Huo, this poor child, I wonder if he has been expelled like me?

The farm behind the garden is now at its peak. Several acres of farmland at home, if you think of coming to this crazy world, you have no blessing. In the countryside, hiring several farmhands to cultivate and plant themselves, life is still more than enough. The winter that hundreds of lives in a village are looking forward to has been warmly welcomed in the countryside before people in our city are aware of it. The rice in the fields, the price of a year's hard work, is piled high in the farm. Those who thresh, those who sift, a few small sparrows who feel that winter has arrived fly and gather in the corner of the field to forage for some wild food. They are all so unafraid of people. However, in Shanghai, there is a competition that is considered a shocking move.

Friends, it is said that Zhao Jie, who looks after ducks next door to us, ran away with someone. A little girl with two braids would also run away with someone, oh, no, Zhao Jie is also the same age as Ah Huo, an eighteen-year-old girl! But where did she run to? East Village? West Village? None of them can be hidden, so I have to ask, is Ah Xiang, the little cobbler, still in our town? He specializes in abducting girls from the countryside and selling them to Shanghai because Shanghai's sins need them to create them. Please tell me, or I can find this child in the pit of fire.

Fantasy is a strange thing. After the five-branched electric light is turned on, what is rolling in my spinal cord is that waist swimming like an eel, the car chasing after the tram, that unusually lovely blind female beggar, the small pavilion building seems to be spinning in a crazy world...

Twelve, at the Xin Sheng small building in October

Amateur Mailbox

Can Interest Be Waived? 263

Editor:

I have a legal question and am asking you for your advice.

The matter is like this: Ten years ago, my father borrowed 800 yuan from someone to fill the losses in the store. At that time, he used the deed of a house as collateral. Needless to say, this money had to pay interest every year; but five or six years ago, my own store closed because it could not be maintained, and as a result, the interest could not be paid and stopped, until now, it has probably been five or six years. Who knew that the creditor suddenly came to live in my current house, which is the house whose deed he had previously used as collateral; no matter what, he refused to move out, and stubbornly wanted money, or wanted us to sell the house to him. As a result, he is still living in the house and has not been resolved.

Therefore, sir, please answer the following questions for me.

(1) The interest on this money has been paid equal to the principal amount. Can the interest that has not been paid in the past few years be waived, legally speaking?

(2) Because he did not pay him back, he forcibly occupied the house. If there was no explicit statement in the original note that he could live in the house if he did not pay back the money, can we now forcibly evict him?

(3) If he does not reason and is simply unreasonable, what steps should be taken to deal with it?

(4) If we meet in court, can we request that the unpaid interest for several years be waived, and the principal be repaid in installments, or reduced by a certain amount? (Because interest equal to the principal has been paid.)

(5) If he is sentenced to repay all of it, what will be the result if he has no money to repay it at that time?

Sir, as a reader, I ask you to give me a satisfactory answer to the above questions. Originally, I am very sorry to bother you with such a boring matter, but who else can give me an answer except you? So I do not hesitate to reveal my ignorance. I am grateful for your help. Sincerely, Xu Hansheng

× × ×

Editor's note: The Civil Code allows and protects interest that does not exceed two cents per month. Because the borrowing period is extended, it is legal for the interest to equal or even exceed the principal. Therefore, Mr. Xu can only negotiate with the other party to make concessions, and not rely on the law.

The original mortgage document did not state clauses such as "If the money is not repaid, you can live in the house"; and the other party actually moved in, which is of course his fault. Mr. Xu can report to the Public Security Bureau and request to stop this infringement; the civil part can be sued to the court again.

But in the end, the court will of course order the principal and interest to be paid in full; if Mr. Xu is unable to pay, he will of course request to seize the mortgaged property. If you say that the value of the house is higher than the amount you should pay, then it can be auctioned off. In short, once the relationship is broken and you meet in court, the debt responsibility cannot be reduced in the slightest.

Therefore, we advocate that Mr. Xu still negotiate with the other party, both the principal and interest, how much he can allow to be reduced is your advantage. There are three ways to pay after the amount is settled: (1) Still mortgage this house to the original creditor. In fact, you only need to take back the old note and create a new one, adding the amount to be equal to the sum of the principal and interest.

(2) Mortgage this house and borrow a sum of money from someone else to deal with this creditor.

(3) Since he wants your house, you should sell it to him reluctantly. When he is happy, on the one hand, he will allow you to reduce the principal and interest, and on the other hand, he will slightly increase the house price, and you will get much more benefit. You must understand that real estate is useless to the poor, and its interest cannot be as high as the interest you pay because of your debt.

P.S. To Mr. Tong Guohua: Please indicate your address, and I will reply by letter.

Novel

Shanghai (2) (6) 264

— Zhang Lao San

(39) Two Legs Frozen Red

This gloomy dusk passed like any other for the celebrities. They ate dinner, smoked, and chatted; but every action seemed constrained. The next day, I sincerely bared my soul to Sister Min in her bedroom. I knew Sister Hui was pursuing me and had put in a great deal of effort for me, but I was determined not to surrender to her. I held Sister Min's hand tightly, wanting to convey to her what I couldn't express in words.

She smiled—a disbelieving smile.

"Sister, remember? Now is not the time for us to be in love," I said, holding her hand even tighter.

She slowly withdrew her hand, lowering her head.

Three days later, Sister Min's attitude was as usual, with talking and laughter. Consequently, everyone's attitude also changed. When Little Huang greeted me, he waved a hand and nodded, awkwardly displaying the air of a burly fellow he aspired to be. When he was carefree, he always imitated Ha-Ha's mannerisms.

Sister Hui didn't come. Seeing how particularly intimate they had been that day, and the changes it brought about, I really wanted to get to the bottom of things with Sister Hui. However, it was better that she didn't come; I should avoid her and let everyone ponder this mystery and arrive at their own conclusions.

The ripples agitated on the water's surface by the stone had gradually calmed, and the water's surface, clear and blue like a mirror, returned to its original state. However, that stone had sunk to the bottom of the river forever. Just like the secrets of the World War, there will always be a day for unveiling.

This day—came on a morning when the cold wind howled, and we were awakened from our sleep by A'fu's trembling cries.

"Mr. Li... Miss Sun... is gone... two rickshaws..."

"When did she leave?" I opened my sleepy eyes and jumped out of bed. This matter seemed to have long been in my calculations, but I was still surprised by the suddenness of it.

"Half a day ago... oh... just left: by rickshaw." A'fu was like an old horse just relieved of a heavy burden, with continuous streams of breath coming out, showing the extent of the cold. "Oh, there's a letter, for Mr. Li," A'fu added.

"Did you hear where the rickshaws went?" I asked, slipping on my slippers, throwing on a coat, and taking the letter from A'fu's hand.

Little Huang heard this and quickly jumped out of bed, darting in front of A'fu, pushing his body and shouting, "Tell me quickly, where did she go? Tell me quickly, quickly!"

"Miss Sun hailed the rickshaws herself, and she gave me this letter in the kitchen. I thought it strange that Miss Sun got up so early today, and when I came out with her, she had already jumped into the rickshaw in front of the door and left."

Little Huang looked back, staring intently at the letter in my hand! An unsealed letter, I sat on the bed, pulled out a piece of foreign paper, filled with scrawled pencil writing. Little Huang slowly walked over, Chongqing and Xiaofeng also sat on my bed with dazed faces, and A'fu also came closer as if drawn by a thread, looking at the letter in my hand; in fact, apart from recognizing his own name, or perhaps only things like "Heaven, Earth, Sun, Moon," he probably knew nothing. However, he stretched his neck, looking so eagerly.

After reading the letter, I collapsed on the bed with a sigh. The letter was taken by Little Huang, who read it word by word, almost stopping his breath.

The cold wind blew through the window, shaking the room around us, making creaking sounds. I felt a chill rising straight up from my heels, I raised my legs, I had not put on woolen socks in my haste, and my two legs were frozen red.

Film Special

A Roll Call of Fame on Hollywood's Pavilion of Outstanding Figures (Part Two) 265

— Xi Rong

A Glimpse of the Achievements of Pioneers in the Film Industry

Six Names to be Inscribed in History and to Endure

(4) Charlie Chaplin: Charlie Chaplin is the greatest figure in contemporary silent film. His greatness lies in his ability to express the plot entirely through action. The agility of the muscles on his face, the stumbling way he walks, the trembling of his hands, are more effective than any words. He can make people experience both sorrow and joy, crying one moment and laughing the next. His performances can represent the journey of a lifetime. We can sympathize with his mistakes and share in his happiness because his actions on the screen are a corner of our daily lives. His performances transcend time and are eternally genuine. He does not belong to a specific time, place, or era. This silent writer has a special talent for portraying the misfortunes of the world's unfortunate people vividly. He gives the failures of the weak a kind of comfort, making them forget pain and worry. Because Charlie Chaplin can reconcile fantasy and reality, he has become an immortal genius artist.

(5) Marie Dressler: She is the epitome of maternal essence in the world. Beneath her clothing and makeup, her health, her sweetness, and her great soul can shine like a beacon in the night. Although she has had great success on the screen, it is minuscule compared to her even greater personal character. Moreover, her life's struggles, up to her late-life glory, can inspire endless hope and encouragement in up-and-coming artists. Many people, when they hear the name Marie Dressler, can associate it with a kind of tender love in their hearts. Her mature life philosophy, combined with her infinite wisdom, allows her to reach directly into the hearts of the audience. Even in her so-called strong-willed performances, her compassion cannot be suppressed. All of this transcends the skill of acting. Furthermore, Marie Dressler is one of the most influential actors in America today. She is also a unique actress in film history, maintaining her star status for many years without losing it. Because she is permanently loved by the people of the United States, her position is also among the immortal.

(6) Greta Garbo: This Swedish megastar's ability to be included among the immortal figures is not due to rumors about her or the various mysteries created around her, but rather because she can arouse the audience's desire while at the same time withholding it, causing them to develop endless admiration. She embodies a substantial temptation, but also, because of her spiritual restraints, suppresses extravagant hopes for close proximity. She flies to the world occasionally, but then flies away in an instant. Her position is inimitable by other film actors. Of course, the feminine qualities she possesses have made her a type that is popular for an entire generation. Therefore, the audience's remembrance of her will also never fade.

Of course, in addition to the six people mentioned above, there are many other big stars who have had impressive works that caused a sensation among people all over the world, but they are all inevitably eliminated by the times and sooner or later become figures of the past. There are also several other great figures who belong to the theater world and not exclusively to the film industry. We can mention the names of George Arliss, Lionel Barrymore, and John Barrymore. Because they did not achieve complete success in the film industry, they are not included among the immortal figures of Hollywood. Of course, there are many other names that could be mentioned in passing, but unfortunately, it is not possible to list them all one by one. (End)

Film Review

Review of "Gallant Flight" 266

— Ling He

Night Flight

Produced by MGM, Premiered at Grand Theater

American films in the past have consistently focused on love affairs, but now, a very serious "Gallant Flight" without many love scenes has suddenly appeared, which can't help but make people feel strange. This may disappoint the audience who are intoxicated in the heat of love.

Everyone will recognize that in the context of a sluggish film business, producers have to do their best to call upon first-class stars. "Grand Hotel" was like this, "Dinner at Eight" was like this, and "Gallant Flight" is also like this. Indeed, when audiences see those famous actors, they will surely have great hope and go to appreciate the film.

However, good actors also need good scripts; otherwise, even stars who can act have no way to develop their talent to the fullest. In addition, when everyone is crowded together, the amount of film allocated to each person in the limited space is very small.

The screenwriter of "Gallant Flight" was indeed very solemn in his creative attitude, but because he was too solemn, he diminished the interest of the play. Of course, we never oppose the solemnity of film, but for people who are not accustomed to it, it still feels unfamiliar.

In any case, there are many commendable features here. It does not exaggerate the fantasies of love, nor does it cater to the audience's low-level interests. It focuses on the center of the story, develops in a very appropriate and positive direction, and has absolutely no perfunctory attitude, which most screenwriters would not dare to do.

We can see traces of different styles from their previous works in several main actors in this film. John Barrymore used to play very emotional roles, and also had a romantic and unrestrained attitude. Emotional roles, such as "The Mad Genius," "State's Attorney," "Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde," and "Grand Hotel," etc. In addition, films such as "Svengali" and "Rasputin and the Empress" also have a mysterious power. But in this film, he plays a very rational character who tries his best to hide his emotions, which further proves that he is a genius actor, a versatile talent. Lionel Barrymore plays a role in this film that is close to a rogue, a confused fool, with an indifferent look, which is also rarely seen before. As for Clark Gable, Helen Hayes, Myrna Loy, and Lionel Barrymore, they still maintain the same style as before.

We feel it is a pity that they do not have the opportunity to act to the fullest. The most regrettable thing is Clark Gable, we can only see the curved part of his face, and there are very few big movements. However, in the few scenes, they are all very delicate and realistic. Especially Helen Hayes can achieve such results in very few scenes, which is really commendable. It can be said that everyone is trying their best to act.

All the techniques are very mature, whether it is lighting, dubbing, or set design, but it is not exaggerated, and it maintains a solemn atmosphere. In particular, the photography of the airplane at night navigating the clouds is extremely beautiful.

So why did the screenwriter use aviation as the background? It is obvious that this kind of theme is still relatively novel. Therefore, some of the knowledge about aviation or radio technology is also introduced. Naturally, this is common scientific knowledge, and it is by no means without benefit to the shallow-minded audience.

Review of "Hips, Hips, Hooray!" 267

— Moore

Although Christmas is a holiday for Europeans and Americans, in Shanghai, where European and American influence is strong, many high-class Chinese also enjoy themselves on this day. Moreover, because the places where they work are closed on this day, the broader masses of the lower class flock to the movie theaters. Therefore, every theater is very crowded on this day, and this cannot be used as a reason to deny the economic crisis.

Wheeler and Woolsey are two actors with the lowest level of taste, and also the least capable. The story of "Hips, Hips, Hooray!" is equally extremely boring. With actors of the lowest level of taste acting in an extremely boring story, the value of "Hips, Hips, Hooray!" is imaginable. Here, we naturally don't need to describe its story.

In the old novel "Journey to the West," we see the story of the Women's Kingdom. At the same time, there is a similar description in "Flowers in the Mirror." "Hips, Hips, Hooray!" is also such a story. However, the location is the well-known Africa. The complete fantasy of this story goes without saying. Its social basis, apart from satisfying human curiosity and stimulating the lewd fantasies of a few people, has no other explanation.

The screenwriter made it clear that this story took place in Africa for a reason: to take advantage of the hot weather in that place. Because the weather is hot, women can wear less clothing. Because the weather is hot, people's personalities are more volatile. At the same time, the heat of the weather, combined with the heat of people's love, can successfully promote "Hips, Hips, Hooray!"

The director firmly grasped the word "hot" in his writing. No matter what, he never forgot the word "hot." Therefore, "Hips, Hips, Hooray!" was successful in terms of atmosphere. It's really impossible to find any other advantages.

As for the performances of the two leading actors, well, there is nothing but acting dumb and foolish. Even the cigar that never lights, I don't know what effect it has other than serving as a personal trademark.

Carl the Mouse, on the other hand, gave the audience considerable satisfaction!

Hollywood's Christmas Preparations 268

— Bing

The annual Christmas holiday is now fast approaching. Those who eagerly look forward to the arrival of Christmas are a group of young rascals in Hollywood. Although they are very young, they will not forget Christmas.

Jackie Cooper is the most efficient child. He has to prepare 30 days before Christmas. Because he gives away a lot of gifts that day, if he doesn't prepare earlier, it will definitely be too late.

Babe Ruth is slightly later than Jackie Cooper in preparing, but he is already preparing his gifts about 25 days before Christmas. Among his gifts, the most valuable are those given to his father and mother, which are probably worth at least several hundred US dollars.

The children's interest is like this, and many older stars are no less than children. Every year on Christmas Day, it's like a stolen day for them. They can't help but make a wild scene, and the gifts they give are also very special. Charlie Chaplin once gave each friend a pair of torn leather shoes. This pair of torn leather shoes was as big as real shoes, like the torn leather shoes he wore in the films, but the raw material was made of chocolate. Jeanette MacDonald once gave each friend a book. The appearance of this book looked like a real book with hundreds of pages, but inside there were only two pages in total. The first page was the name of the giver and receiver, and the second page was a poem celebrating Christmas and the New Year, and this book was also made of sugar, and the outer book cover was exactly a box. This year, I don't know what new methods these many stars are thinking of.

"The Price of Love" Opens Today in Beijing 269

— Tian Zhang

The year 1933 can indeed be called a movie year. Not only did several large companies with strong capital desperately produce many new films, but also many small companies with weak capital and lack of talent worked hard to produce many works to catch up with the times.

Recently, Tianbei Company, a small company, after a long period of struggle, rushed to produce a new film called "The Price of Love," which will open today at the Beijing Grand Theater.

This refers to how a weak woman bound by the old marriage system of modern society resists her environment and lives by her own efforts. As a result, under hypocrisy and deception, a tragedy of loyalty and love under the capitalist system is created.

In the deformed society of modern times, the love that every young person experiences has indeed become an important issue at the center of society. "The Price of Love" is to provide society with materials for studying this issue, so this film is well worth introducing.

Film Novel

Shanghai 24 Hours (5) 270

— Tian Fu

At this time, Lao Zhao was pacing outside the compradore's mansion. A sneaking rat was tempting his heart, and hunger was emboldening him: he finally slipped into the compradore's mansion like a shadow. Not long after, the wife, returning from a leisurely outing, had already leaned in the youth's arms and been sent back to the mansion by car, preparing to begin her sweet dreams.

(7) Thief

The compradore's wife was a little tired and needed rest, but a negligee was missing. Searching, she couldn't find it; she discovered muddy footprints on the floor. Thus, a small commotion arose in the house. The wife angrily blamed the compradore, searching the jewelry box to see what was missing; the compradore got out of bed groggily, blaming the maid for being negligent; Lao Chen's wife stood beside him in a daze, her face full of panic... The wife called the police station, and the police station then sent a detective.

"A negligee, a brooch inlaid with precious stones. Stolen after 2:00 AM last night," the compradore's wife told the detective. The detective then went to examine the footprints that the grumpy dog was sniffing on the floor. He then asked the wife: "Besides the servants, have any other suspicious people come here in the past few days?"

The wife thought, her eyes suddenly glaring at Chen's wife, as if to nail her to death with her gaze. "That's right, it must have something to do with her!" the wife said to the detective, pointing at Chen's wife: "Yesterday evening, her husband was talking to her sneakily in the gatehouse." So the detective took Chen's wife: "to the station to talk."

"To the station to talk": Although you can talk; whether they believe you is their business. You say you didn't steal anything? They say nonsense, you dare to deny it after being a thief! Anyway, poor people are not good people, you have to lock them up and fix them: this is the rule! Lao Chen really did talk to his wife in the gatehouse of the Zhou mansion last night, and this is a 100% major suspicion. So Chen's wife was forced to take them to the small vegetable market, and they arrested Lao Chen. "To the station", lock him up and fix him.

(8) Secret Under the Sun

It was 7:00 or 8:00 in the morning, and the sunlight was shining brightly on this bustling city again. It is said that all secret actions or crimes are carried out in the dark. Here we want to introduce a little secret in broad daylight under the sun. Of course, Lao Zhao's stealing is a crime. Strangely enough, Lao Zhao couldn't help but feel ashamed of his crime, but he was also a little happy. The person who "commits the crime" does so because he has "suffered" too much. When poor people have nowhere to turn, they often have to "commit a crime" to save their lives. Lao Zhao was so poor that committing a crime made his spirits much more active. The first job in the morning was naturally to go to the pawnshop to exchange the negligee and brooch for money. There were people starving at home, and countless letters asking for money had arrived; now he had to send three or five yuan back: so he went to the post office. The panic in his stomach had to be resolved. What else? Oh! Chen Da's younger brother was too pitiful, he was injured and had no money to hire a doctor; the suffering of the poor can only be understood by the poor, could he, Lao Zhao, not help since he had money? There were two yuan left in his hand, so he used these two yuan to hire a doctor to treat Lao Chen's younger brother...(To be continued)
